Croatian (Hrvatski) — content review

Corlang course content for native-speaker review. Please mark any translation, spelling, grammar, or naturalness issues in the “Correction / notes” spaces. The bold term is the Croatian; the grey text is the English.

1. Vocabulary (2566 words)

First conversations A1

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
Kako si?How are you? (informal)formal: Kako ste?
Kako se zoveš?What's your name? (informal)
Ja sam…I am… (name, nationality, state)
Drago mi je.Nice to meet you.
Odakle si?Where are you from?Ja sam iz… + genitive
Koliko košta?How much does it cost?
Gdje je…?Where is…?
Živjeli!Cheers!
Sretno!Good luck!
Dobar tek!Enjoy your meal!distinctly Croatian (vs 'prijatno')
Vidimo se!See you!
Sve najbolje!All the best!

Professions & occupations A1

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
zanimanjeprofession / occupationn. n.also means 'interest' (zanimanje za + accusative)Koje je tvoje zanimanje?
What is your profession?
liječnicadoctor (female)n. f.masculine: liječnik; distinctly Croatian (vs colloquial 'doktorica')Moja sestra je liječnica.
My sister is a doctor.
medicinska sestranurse (female)n. f.male nurse: medicinski tehničarMedicinska sestra radi u bolnici.
The nurse works in a hospital.
učiteljteacher (primary school, male)n. m.feminine: učiteljica; secondary school and university: profesorNaš učitelj je jako ljubazan.
Our teacher is very kind.
učiteljicateacher (primary school, female)n. f.Učiteljica objašnjava novu lekciju.
The teacher explains the new lesson.
profesorprofessor / secondary-school teachern. m.feminine: profesoricaProfesor predaje matematiku.
The professor teaches mathematics.
inženjerengineern. m.feminine: inženjerkaMoj brat je inženjer.
My brother is an engineer.
konobarwaitern. m.feminine: konobaricaKonobar donosi dvije kave.
The waiter is bringing two coffees.
konobaricawaitressn. f.Konobarica radi u restoranu.
The waitress works in a restaurant.
kuharcook / chefn. m.feminine: kuharicaKuhar kuha ukusnu juhu.
The cook is making a tasty soup.
vozačdrivern. m.feminine: vozačicaVozač vozi autobus po gradu.
The driver drives the bus around town.
policajacpolice officern. m.genitive: policajca (fleeting a); feminine: policajkaPolicajac stoji na ulici.
The police officer is standing in the street.
vatrogasacfirefightern. m.genitive: vatrogasca (fleeting a)Vatrogasac gasi vatru.
The firefighter is putting out the fire.
odvjetniklawyern. m.distinctly Croatian (vs 'advokat'); feminine: odvjetnicaTrebam dobrog odvjetnika.
I need a good lawyer.
prodavačsalesperson / shop assistantn. m.feminine: prodavačicaProdavač radi u trgovini.
The salesperson works in a shop.
frizerhairdressern. m.feminine: frizerkaFrizer mi šiša kosu.
The hairdresser is cutting my hair.
pekarbakern. m.pekarnica = bakeryPekar peče svježi kruh.
The baker bakes fresh bread.
mesarbutchern. m.mesnica = butcher's shopMesar prodaje svježe meso.
The butcher sells fresh meat.
zubardentistn. m.standard also: stomatolog; feminine: zubarkaSutra idem zubaru.
Tomorrow I'm going to the dentist.
novinarjournalistn. m.feminine: novinarka; novine = newspaperNovinar piše za novine.
The journalist writes for a newspaper.
glumacactorn. m.genitive: glumca; feminine: glumicaGlumac radi u kazalištu.
The actor works in the theatre.
pjevačsingern. m.feminine: pjevačicaPjevač pjeva lijepu pjesmu.
The singer sings a beautiful song.
glazbenikmusiciann. m.distinctly Croatian (vs 'muzičar'); glazba = musicGlazbenik svira gitaru.
The musician plays the guitar.
sportašathleten. m.distinctly Croatian (vs 'sportista'); feminine: sportašicaSportaš trenira svaki dan.
The athlete trains every day.
poljoprivrednikfarmern. m.Poljoprivrednik radi na selu.
The farmer works in the countryside.
ribarfishermann. m.Ribar lovi ribu na moru.
The fisherman catches fish at sea.
tajnicasecretary (female)n. f.masculine: tajnikTajnica organizira sastanke.
The secretary organizes the meetings.
znanstvenikscientistn. m.distinctly Croatian (vs 'naučnik'); feminine: znanstvenicaZnanstvenik radi na sveučilištu.
The scientist works at the university.
arhitektarchitectn. m.feminine: arhitekticaArhitekt crta plan kuće.
The architect draws the house plan.
programerprogrammern. m.feminine: programerkaProgramer cijeli dan radi na računalu.
The programmer works on the computer all day.
poduzetnikentrepreneurn. m.feminine: poduzetnicaPoduzetnik ima svoju tvrtku.
The entrepreneur has his own company.
radnikworkern. m.feminine: radnicaRadnik počinje posao u sedam.
The worker starts work at seven.
studentuniversity student (male)n. m.only for university; school pupil = učenikStudent uči za ispit.
The student is studying for an exam.
studenticauniversity student (female)n. f.Studentica živi u Zagrebu.
The student lives in Zagreb.
umirovljenikpensioner / retireen. m.distinctly Croatian (vs 'penzioner'); feminine: umirovljenicaMoj djed je umirovljenik.
My grandfather is a pensioner.
domaćicahousewifen. f.also means 'hostess'Domaćica kuha ručak za obitelj.
The housewife cooks lunch for the family.
vojniksoldiern. m.vojska = armyVojnik nosi uniformu.
The soldier wears a uniform.
svećenikpriestn. m.distinctly Croatian (vs 'sveštenik')Svećenik radi u našoj crkvi.
The priest works in our church.
poštarpostmann. m.pošta = post officePoštar donosi pisma svaki dan.
The postman brings letters every day.
taksisttaxi drivern. m.Taksist vozi po cijelom gradu.
The taxi driver drives all over the city.
blagajnicacashier (female)n. f.masculine: blagajnik; blagajna = cash register / tillBlagajnica broji novac.
The cashier is counting the money.
direktordirector / managern. m.feminine: direktoricaDirektor ima sastanak u deset.
The director has a meeting at ten.
zaposlenemployedadj.also 'busy' in colloquial use; zaposlena (f)Brat mi je zaposlen u bolnici.
My brother is employed at the hospital.
nezaposlenunemployedadj.opposite: zaposlenOn je sada nezaposlen.
He is unemployed at the moment.
raditi kaoto work asphrasefollowed by the nominative: radim kao konobarRadim kao konobar u hotelu.
I work as a waiter in a hotel.

Personality, appearance & emotions A1

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
osobapersonn. f.grammatically feminine even when referring to a manOna je vrlo dobra osoba.
She is a very good person.
pametansmart / cleveradj.pametna (f), fleeting aOn je pametan dječak.
He is a smart boy.
glupstupidadj.To je glupa ideja.
That is a stupid idea.
ljubazankind / politeadj.ljubazna (f), fleeting aProdavačica je uvijek ljubazna.

dragdear / sweetadj.Draga Ana = Dear Ana (letters); drag mi je = I like himOna mi je jako draga.
I like her a lot.

The film was very boring.

Father is angry with me.

The mother is worried about her son.
ponosanproudadj.ponosan na + accusative; ponosna (f)Ponosan sam na svoju djecu.

His story is very funny.
duhovitwitty / humorousadj.Moj prijatelj je vrlo duhovit.

hrabarbraveadj.hrabra (f), fleeting aVatrogasci su hrabri ljudi.

mirancalm / quietadj.mirna (f), fleeting a; mir = peaceOn je miran i tih čovjek.
He is a calm and quiet man.
nervozannervousadj.nervozna (f), fleeting aPrije ispita sam uvijek nervozan.
Before an exam I am always nervous.
tihquiet / silentadj.Ona je tiha osoba.
She is a quiet person.
glasanloudadj.glasna (f), fleeting aDjeca su danas glasna.
The children are loud today.
otvorenopen (person or thing)adj.of people: outgoing, open-mindedOna je otvorena i vesela osoba.
She is an open and cheerful person.
simpatičanlikeable / niceadj.simpatična (f), fleeting aNova kolegica je jako simpatična.
The new colleague is very likeable.
zgodanhandsome / good-lookingadj.zgodna (f); also means 'handy / convenient'On je zgodan mladić.
He is a handsome young man.
visoktall / highadj.comparative: višiMoj brat je vrlo visok.
My brother is very tall.
nizakshort (height) / lowadj.niska (f), fleeting a; comparative: nižiOna je niska, ali jako brza.
She is short but very fast.
mršavthin / skinnyadj.Taj pas je jako mršav.
That dog is very skinny.
debeofat / thickadj.debela (f), debelo (n), l/o alternationNaš mačak je debeo i lijen.

jakstrongadj.also of coffee/tea: jaka kava = strong coffeeVojnik mora biti jak.
A soldier must be strong.
slabweakadj.Djed je star i slab.
Grandpa is old and weak.
osjećajfeelingn. m.Imam dobar osjećaj.
I have a good feeling.
ljubavloven. f.feminine despite the consonant ending (i-declension)Ljubav je najvažnija stvar u životu.
Love is the most important thing in life.
strahfearn. m.strah od + genitive; Strah me je. = I'm scared.Osjećam strah prije ispita.
I feel fear before the exam.
radostjoyn. f.nouns ending in -ost are feminineDjeca skaču od radosti.
The children are jumping for joy.
srećahappiness / luckn. f.imati sreće = to be luckyNovac ne može kupiti sreću.
Money cannot buy happiness.
tugasadnessn. f.Njegova pjesma je puna tuge.
His song is full of sadness.
brigaworry / caren. f.Ne brini! = Don't worry!Imam puno briga na poslu.

nadahopen. f.Nada umire posljednja.
Hope dies last. (proverb)
bojati seto be afraidv. impf.bojim se; takes the genitive: bojim se mrakaBojim se velikih pasa.
I am afraid of big dogs.
nadati seto hopev. impf.nadam se; takes the dativeNadam se dobroj ocjeni.
I am hoping for a good grade.
veseliti seto look forward tov. impf.takes the dative: veselim se ljetuVeselim se ljetu i moru.
I am looking forward to summer and the sea.

Daily routine verbs III A1

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
ustajatito get up (habitually)v. impf.ustajem; pf. partner: ustatiUstajem svaki dan u sedam.
I get up every day at seven.
ustatito get upv. pf.ustanem; impf. partner: ustajatiJučer sam ustao u šest.
Yesterday I got up at six.
buditi seto wake up (habitually)v. impf.pf. partner: probuditi seBudim se rano ujutro.
I wake up early in the morning.
probuditi seto wake upv. pf.impf. partner: buditi seProbudio sam se u osam.
I woke up at eight.
tuširati seto take a showerv. impf.pf. partner: istuširati seTuširam se svako jutro.
I take a shower every morning.
pratito washv. impf.perem; pf. partner: opratiPerem zube svaku večer.
I brush my teeth every evening.
oblačiti seto get dressed (habitually)v. impf.pf. partner: obući seBrzo se oblačim prije posla.
I get dressed quickly before work.
obući seto get dressedv. pf.obučem se; imperative: obuci se; impf. partner: oblačiti seObuci se, idemo van!
Get dressed, we're going out!
doručkovatito have breakfastv. impf.doručkujemDoručkujem kruh, sir i jaje.
For breakfast I have bread, cheese and an egg.
ručatito have lunchv. impf.biaspectual, works as both impf. and pf.Nedjeljom ručamo kod bake.
On Sundays we have lunch at grandma's.
večeratito have dinnerv. impf.biaspectual, works as both impf. and pf.Večeramo zajedno u osam.
We have dinner together at eight.
žuritito hurryv. impf.often reflexive: žuriti se; pf. partner: požuritiŽurim na posao, vidimo se!
I'm hurrying to work, see you!
kasnitito be late / run latev. impf.pf. partner: zakasnitiAutobus opet kasni deset minuta.
The bus is ten minutes late again.
zakasnitito be late / miss (by lateness)v. pf.zakasniti na + accusative; impf. partner: kasnitiZakasnio sam na sastanak.
I was late for the meeting.
stizatito arrive (habitually)v. impf.stižem; pf. partner: stićiVlak stiže u pet sati.
The train arrives at five o'clock.
stićito arrivev. pf.stignem; past: stigao/stigla; impf. partner: stizatiStigli smo kući jako kasno.
We arrived home very late.
dolazitito come (habitually)v. impf.pf. partner: doćiDolazim kući oko šest.
I come home around six.
odlazitito leave (habitually)v. impf.pf. partner: otićiOdlazim na posao u osam.
I leave for work at eight.

Adverbs of intensity & manner A2

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
vrloveryadv.slightly more formal than jakoOna je vrlo ljubazna.

jakovery, stronglyadv.from the adjective jak (strong)Jako mi se sviđa ovaj film.

Connectors & sentence glue A2

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
dokwhileconj.Dok kuham, slušam radio.
While I cook, I listen to the radio.
čimas soon asconj.Nazvat ću te čim stignem kući.
I'll call you as soon as I get home.
prije nego štobefore (doing something)conj.introduces a clause; compare prije + genitiveOperi ruke prije nego što jedeš.
Wash your hands before you eat.
nakon štoafter (doing something)conj.introduces a clause; compare nakon + genitiveNakon što smo večerali, gledali smo film.
After we had dinner, we watched a film.
iakoalthough, even thoughconj.Iako pada kiša, idemo u šetnju.
Although it's raining, we're going for a walk.
premdaalthough (formal)conj.synonym: iakoPremda je umoran, još radi.
Although he is tired, he is still working.
budući dasince, given thatconj.gives a reason; more formal than jerBudući da nemam auto, idem vlakom.
Since I don't have a car, I'm going by train.
zato štobecauseconj.answers zašto?; synonym: jerUčim hrvatski zato što volim Hrvatsku.
I'm learning Croatian because I love Croatia.
tako daso (that), with the result thatconj.Kasnio je autobus, tako da sam zakasnio na posao.
The bus was late, so I was late for work.
kako biin order to, so thatconj.bi changes with the subject: kako bih, kako bismo...Štedim novac kako bih kupio stan.
I'm saving money in order to buy a flat.
umjesto dainstead of (doing)conj.compare umjesto + genitive with nounsUmjesto da učiš, gledaš televiziju.
Instead of studying, you're watching TV.
osimexcept, besidesprep.+ genitiveSvi su došli osim Marka.
Everyone came except Marko.
osim togabesides, moreoverphraseStan je lijep; osim toga, blizu je centra.
The flat is nice; besides, it's close to the centre.
dakletherefore, soconj.Karta je skupa, dakle idemo pješice.
The ticket is expensive, so we're walking.
stogatherefore (formal)conj.synonym: zato, daklePada snijeg, stoga vozite polako.
It's snowing, therefore drive slowly.
zatimthen, afterwardsadv.synonym: onda, potomPrvo doručkujemo, zatim idemo van.
First we have breakfast, then we go out.
potomafterwards (formal)adv.synonym: zatimPročitaj tekst, potom odgovori na pitanja.
Read the text, then answer the questions.
naimenamely, you seeadv.introduces an explanationNe mogu doći; naime, radim u subotu.
I can't come; you see, I work on Saturday.
primjericefor instanceadv.synonym: na primjerVolim sport, primjerice plivanje i tenis.
I like sport, for instance swimming and tennis.
na primjerfor examplephraseabbreviated npr.Jedem puno voća, na primjer jabuke i banane.
I eat a lot of fruit, for example apples and bananas.
s jedne straneon the one handphrasepairs with s druge straneS jedne strane volim grad, s druge mi nedostaje priroda.
On the one hand I love the city, on the other I miss nature.
s druge straneon the other handphrasePosao je težak; s druge strane, plaća je dobra.
The job is hard; on the other hand, the pay is good.
prvofirst, firstlyadv.Prvo moramo kupiti karte.
First we have to buy the tickets.
drugosecond, secondlyadv.Prvo, nemam vremena; drugo, nemam novca.
First, I have no time; second, I have no money.
na krajuin the end, finallyphraseNa kraju smo ipak našli hotel.
In the end we found a hotel after all.
ukratkoin short, brieflyadv.Ukratko, putovanje je bilo odlično.
In short, the trip was excellent.
to jestthat is (i.e.)phraseabbreviated tj.Dolazim za tjedan dana, to jest u petak.
I'm coming in a week, that is, on Friday.
ni … nineither … norconj.verb is negated too: ne pijem ni... ni...Ne pijem ni kavu ni čaj.
I drink neither coffee nor tea.
ili … ilieither … orconj.Ili idemo sada ili ćemo zakasniti.
Either we go now or we'll be late.
i … iboth … andconj.Govori i engleski i njemački.
She speaks both English and German.
što se tičeas far as … is concernedphrase+ genitive: što se tiče cijeneŠto se tiče cijene, sve je u redu.
As far as the price is concerned, everything is fine.
u vezi sin connection with, regardingphrase+ instrumentalZovem u vezi s oglasom za stan.
I'm calling about the advertisement for the flat.
zbogbecause ofprep.+ genitiveZbog kiše nismo išli na izlet.
Because of the rain we didn't go on the trip.
zbog togabecause of that, that's whyphraseNisam spavao i zbog toga sam umoran.
I didn't sleep and that's why I'm tired.
unatočdespite, in spite ofprep.+ dative: unatoč kišiUnatoč kiši, utakmica se igrala.
Despite the rain, the match was played.
aand, whereas (mild contrast)conj.contrasts two statements; softer than aliJa pijem kavu, a on pije čaj.
I drink coffee, and he drinks tea.
negobut (rather); thanconj.after negation: ne X, nego Y; also in comparisonsNije plav, nego zelen.
It's not blue but green.
takođeralso, as welladv.Ja također volim more.
I also love the sea.
kaoas, likeconj.Hladno je kao zimi.
It's cold like in winter.
kao štoas, just asconj.introduces a clauseSve je prošlo kao što smo planirali.
Everything went as we planned.
bez obzira naregardless ofphrase+ accusativeIdemo na izlet bez obzira na vrijeme.
We're going on the trip regardless of the weather.
u svakom slučajuin any casephraseU svakom slučaju, javit ću ti se sutra.
In any case, I'll get in touch with you tomorrow.
prije svegaabove all, first of allphrasePrije svega, hvala vam na pomoći.
First of all, thank you for your help.
otkadsince (a point in time)conj.also otkadaOtkad živim ovdje, osjećam se bolje.
Since I've been living here, I feel better.
drugim riječimain other wordsphraseKasno je; drugim riječima, moramo ići.
It's late; in other words, we have to go.

Verb families & aspect pairs B1

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
napisatito write (down), finish writingv. pf.pf. partner of pisati; use for a completed piece of writingNapisala sam pismo baki.
I wrote a letter to my grandmother.
opisati / opisivatito describev. pf./impf.aspect pair; opisati = describe once/completely, opisivati = repeatedly or in progress; takes accusativeMožeš li mi opisati svoj stan?
Can you describe your apartment to me?
zapisati / zapisivatito write down, notev. pf./impf.za- = fix in writing so you don't forget; zapisati broj/adresuZapisao sam tvoj broj telefona u bilježnicu.
I wrote your phone number down in a notebook.
ispisatito write out; to print outv. pf.iz- = out; ispisati se = withdraw one's enrollment (opposite of upisati se)Učiteljica je ispisala nove riječi na ploču.
The teacher wrote the new words out on the board.
dopisatito add (in writing)v. pf.do- = add on to something already written; cf. dopisivati se = to correspond (separate card)Dopisao je rečenicu na kraj teksta.
He added a sentence at the end of the text.
dopisivati seto correspond, exchange messagesv. impf.reflexive; s + instrumental: dopisujem se s prijateljemGodinama se dopisujem s prijateljicom iz Splita.
I have been corresponding with a friend from Split for years.
upisati se / upisivati seto enroll, registerv. pf./impf.u + accusative: upisati se na tečaj/fakultet; opposite: ispisati seUpisala sam se na tečaj hrvatskog jezika.
I enrolled in a Croatian language course.
prepisati / prepisivatito copy (a text); to prescribev. pf./impf.pre- = over/across: copy from a source; liječnik prepisuje lijek = the doctor prescribes medicinePrepisao je zadaću od kolege iz razreda.
He copied the homework from a classmate.
pogledatito take a look, have a look atv. pf.pf. partner of gledati; pogledati film = watch a film (to the end)Pogledaj ovu fotografiju s putovanja!
Take a look at this photo from the trip!
pregledati / pregledavatito examine, check, reviewv. pf./impf.pre- = go through item by item: a doctor examines a patient, a teacher checks tests; noun pregledLiječnik je pregledao pacijenta i prepisao mu lijek.
The doctor examined the patient and prescribed him medicine.
razgledati / razgledavatito sightsee, look aroundv. pf./impf.raz- = look around in all directions: razgledati grad/muzejJučer smo razgledali centar Zagreba.
Yesterday we looked around the centre of Zagreb.
ugledatito catch sight of, spotv. pf.sudden, unplanned perception; cf. pogledati = look deliberatelyU gužvi sam ugledao staru prijateljicu.
In the crowd I caught sight of an old friend.
nadgledatito supervise, overseev. impf.nad- = over (watch from above); no common pf. partnerŠef nadgleda rad novih radnika.
The boss supervises the work of the new workers.
izgledatito look, appear, seemv. impf.izgledaš umorno = you look tired; izgleda da... = it seems that...; noun izgledDanas izgledaš jako umorno.
You look very tired today.
zagledati seto fix one's gaze on; to fall for someonev. pf.u + accusative: zagledao se u nju = he stared at her / fell for herZagledala se u izlog trgovine.
She fixed her gaze on the shop window.
pomislitito think (of), have a sudden thoughtv. pf.momentary thought; na + accusative: pomisliti na nekogaKad čujem more, pomislim na djetinjstvo.
When I hear the sea, I think of my childhood.
izmisliti / izmišljatito invent, make upv. pf./impf.invent a story, excuse or device; ne izmišljaj! = don't make things up!; cf. smisliti = think up (a plan)Izmislio je priču da ne mora doći.
He made up a story so he wouldn't have to come.
razmisliti / razmišljatito think over / to reflectv. pf./impf.o + locative: razmišljam o poslu; razmisliti = finish thinking and be ready to decideMoram razmisliti o tvojoj ponudi do sutra.
I have to think over your offer by tomorrow.
zamisliti / zamišljatito imaginev. pf./impf.zamisli! = imagine!; zamisliti se = become pensiveZamisli da živimo na otoku!
Imagine that we live on an island!
umisliti sito get (an idea) into one's head, imagine falselyv. pf.pejorative; si = dative reflexive; umislio si je da je najbolji = he thinks he's the bestUmislio si je da svi govore o njemu.
He got it into his head that everyone talks about him.
smisliti / smišljatito think up, devisev. pf./impf.smisliti plan/rješenje; cf. izmisliti = invent, especially something untrueSmislili smo dobar plan za vikend.
We thought up a good plan for the weekend.
predomisliti seto change one's mindv. pf.impf. predomišljati se = keep hesitatingHtio je doći, ali se predomislio.
He wanted to come, but he changed his mind.
uraditito do (and finish)v. pf.pf. of raditi; in everyday Croatian napraviti is more commonSve što je obećao, to je i uradio.
Everything he promised, he actually did.
napravitito make, dov. pf.the everyday pf. partner of raditi/praviti: napraviti grešku/kolač/redNapravila sam kolač za rođendan.
I made a cake for the birthday.
odraditi / odrađivatito work off, get (a task) donev. pf./impf.od- = complete an obligation: odraditi smjenu/posaoOdradio je smjenu i otišao kući.
He worked his shift and went home.
preraditi / prerađivatito process, reworkv. pf./impf.pre- = transform: prerađivati voće/ribu; preraditi tekst = rework a textU toj tvornici prerađuju ribu.
In that factory they process fish.
razraditito work out in detail, elaboratev. pf.razraditi plan/ideju; impf. razrađivatiMoramo detaljno razraditi plan puta.
We have to work out the travel plan in detail.
obraditi / obrađivatito process, cover, work on (a topic, data, land)v. pf./impf.obraditi lekciju = cover a lesson; obrađivati podatke/zemljuNa satu smo obradili novu lekciju.
In class we covered a new lesson.
izraditi / izrađivatito make, produce, craftv. pf./impf.more 'craft/produce' than napraviti: izraditi nakit/dokumentOna izrađuje nakit od morskog stakla.
She makes jewellery from sea glass.
surađivatito cooperate, collaboratev. impf.su- = together + raditi; s + instrumental: surađujem s kolegama; noun suradnjaNaša škola surađuje s fakultetom u Zagrebu.
Our school cooperates with a faculty in Zagreb.
zvati (se)to call; (se) to be calledv. impf.zovem, zoveš...; zvati na kavu = invite for coffee; pf. partners are prefixed: pozvati, nazvatiZovem se Ana, a kako se ti zoveš?
My name is Ana, and what is your name?
nazivatito call (on the phone, repeatedly); to namev. impf.impf. partner of nazvati (already learned); nazivati stvari pravim imenom = call things by their real nameNaziva me svaki dan poslije posla.
He calls me every day after work.
odazvati se / odazivati seto respond (to a call or invitation)v. pf./impf.takes dative: odazvati se pozivuMnogi su se odazvali pozivu za pomoć.
Many responded to the call for help.
izazvati / izazivatito cause, provoke; to challengev. pf./impf.izazvati požar/reakciju = cause; izazvati nekoga = challenge someone; noun izazovOluja je izazvala velike probleme u prometu.
The storm caused big problems in traffic.
statito stop; to step; to fit (into)v. pf.present stanem, staneš (B1 pattern -ati > -anem); sve ne stane u torbu = it all doesn't fit in the bagAutobus je stao ispred škole.
The bus stopped in front of the school.
postati / postajatito becomev. pf./impf.postao je liječnik; postaje hladno = it is getting coldNakon studija postala je učiteljica.
After her studies she became a teacher.
ostati / ostajatito stay, remainv. pf./impf.ostati kod kuće; ostalo je malo vremena = little time remains; do not confuse with ostaviti = leave something behindVečeras ostajem kod kuće jer pada kiša.
Tonight I am staying home because it is raining.
pristatito agree (to), consentv. pf.na + accusative: pristati na prijedlog; its impf. pristajati you already know as 'to suit/fit', same verb, second meaningNa kraju je pristala na naš prijedlog.
In the end she agreed to our proposal.
prestati / prestajatito stop, cease (doing something)v. pf./impf.+ infinitive: prestani pričati!; kiša je prestala = the rain stoppedKiša je napokon prestala padati.
The rain finally stopped falling.
nastati / nastajatito come into being, arisev. pf./impf.nastao je problem = a problem arose; grad je nastao u srednjem vijekuTako je nastala naša najpoznatija pjesma.
That is how our most famous song came into being.
zastatito pause, stop for a momentv. pf.brief stop, then you continue; cf. stati = stop (fully)Zastao je na trenutak i pogledao more.
He paused for a moment and looked at the sea.
izostati / izostajatito be absent; to fail to happenv. pf./impf.izostati s nastave = miss class (s + genitive); rezultat nije izostao = the result did not fail to comeZbog bolesti je izostao s nastave tri dana.
Because of illness he was absent from class for three days.
odustati / odustajatito give up, withdrawv. pf./impf.od + genitive: odustati od plana/studijaNemoj odustati od svog sna!
Don't give up on your dream!
sastati se / sastajati seto meet (by arrangement)v. pf./impf.s + instrumental; noun sastanak (already known)Sastat ćemo se sutra ispred kazališta.
We will meet tomorrow in front of the theatre.
postojatito existv. impf.postoji/postoje = there is/there are; no pf. partnerPostoji li ovdje neki dobar restoran?
Is there a good restaurant here?
držatito hold, keepv. impf.držati riječ = keep one's word; držati do sebe = have self-respect; base of a large B1 familyMajka drži dijete za ruku.
The mother holds the child by the hand.
izdržatito endure, hold outv. pf.impf. izdržavati also means 'to support financially' (izdržavati obitelj)Ne mogu više izdržati ovu vrućinu.
I can't stand this heat any longer.
zadržati / zadržavatito keep, retain; to hold up (delay)v. pf./impf.zadržati kartu = keep the ticket; zadržati se = stay longer than plannedOprostite, zadržao me posao u uredu.
Sorry, work at the office held me up.
održati / održavatito hold (an event); to maintainv. pf./impf.održati sastanak/govor/obećanje; održavati kuću/vezu = maintain; održati se = take placeKoncert će se održati na glavnom trgu.
The concert will be held on the main square.
podržati / podržavatito support (an idea, a person)v. pf./impf.takes accusative: podržati prijedlog/prijatelja; noun podrškaObitelj me podržava u svemu.
My family supports me in everything.
pridržatito hold (for a moment)v. pf.pridržati vrata/torbu; pridržavati se + genitive = abide by (pravila = the rules)Možeš li mi pridržati torbu na trenutak?
Can you hold my bag for a moment?
zaigratito start playing; to play (once)v. pf.za- = begin: zaigrati za momčad = start playing for a teamNapokon je zaigrao za prvu momčad.
He finally started playing for the first team.
odigratito play out (a match, a role) to the endv. pf.od- = complete: odigrati utakmicu/uloguMomčad je odigrala odličnu utakmicu.
The team played an excellent match.
razigrati seto get carried away playing, come alive in playv. pf.raz- + se = fully enter the activity; also of a team finding its rhythmDjeca su se razigrala u parku.
The children got carried away playing in the park.
poigrati seto play around (with), toy withv. pf.s + instrumental, often figurative: poigrati se s osjećajima; impf. poigravati seNetko se poigrao s mojim stvarima.
Someone has been playing around with my things.
izigratito outplay; to betray (trust), get around (rules)v. pf.izigrati pravila/povjerenje; impf. izigravati also = to act/pretend (izigravati žrtvu)Izigrao je povjerenje svojih kolega.
He betrayed the trust of his colleagues.
doživjeti / doživljavatito experiencev. pf./impf.doživjeti uspjeh/nezgodu; doživjeti stotu = live to be a hundred; noun doživljajNa putovanju smo doživjeli pravu avanturu.
On the trip we experienced a real adventure.
preživjeti / preživljavatito survivev. pf./impf.pre- = through: live through something; colloquially also 'to get by'Svi su putnici preživjeli nesreću.
All the passengers survived the accident.
nadživjetito outlivev. pf.nad- = beyond: live longer than someoneBaka je nadživjela sve svoje prijateljice.
Grandma outlived all her friends.
uživjeti seto immerse oneself (in a role or situation)v. pf.u + accusative: uživjeti se u uloguGlumac se potpuno uživio u ulogu.
The actor completely immersed himself in the role.
oživjeti / oživljavatito revive, come (back) to lifev. pf./impf.the pf. present is used habitually here: grad oživi ljeti = the town comes alive in summerStari grad oživi svakog ljeta.
The old town comes alive every summer.
uživatito enjoyv. impf.u + locative: uživam u glazbi; same root živ- (living)Uživamo u šetnji uz more.
We enjoy a walk along the sea.
dogovoriti se / dogovarati seto agree, arrange (with someone)v. pf./impf.dogovoriti se o + locative or za + accusative; noun dogovorDogovorili smo se za sastanak u petak.
We arranged a meeting for Friday.
nagovoriti / nagovaratito persuade, talk (someone) intov. pf./impf.nagovoriti koga na + accusative or da + clausePrijatelji su me nagovorili da dođem.
My friends talked me into coming.
ogovaratito gossip aboutv. impf.takes a direct object (accusative): ogovarati susjedeNije lijepo ogovarati kolege s posla.
It's not nice to gossip about colleagues from work.
prigovoriti / prigovaratito object; to nag, complain (to someone)v. pf./impf.takes dative: stalno mi prigovara = he/she keeps nagging meUvijek mi prigovara zbog nereda u sobi.
She always nags me about the mess in my room.
progovoritito start speaking; to speak upv. pf.dijete je progovorilo = the child said its first words; progovoriti o problemu = finally speak up about itDijete je progovorilo s godinu dana.
The child started speaking at one year old.
pustiti / puštatito let, let go, releasev. pf./impf.base pair of the -pustiti family; pusti me! = let me go!; pustiti glazbu = put on musicPustili su psa da trči po plaži.
They let the dog run on the beach.
dopustiti / dopuštatito allow, permitv. pf./impf.+ dative + da: dopustili su mi da ostanem = they allowed me to stayRoditelji su joj dopustili da izađe.
Her parents allowed her to go out.
ispustiti / ispuštatito drop; to emit; to leave outv. pf./impf.ispustiti čašu = drop a glass; ispustiti riječ = omit a wordIspustila je čašu i razbila je.
She dropped the glass and broke it.
popustiti / popuštatito give in, yield; to ease offv. pf./impf.popustiti pod pritiskom = give in under pressure; bol popušta = the pain is easingNa kraju je otac popustio i kupio psa.
In the end the father gave in and bought a dog.
propustiti / propuštatito miss (a chance, a bus); to let throughv. pf./impf.propustiti priliku/vlak; propustiti nekoga naprijed = let someone pass; not the same as otpustiti = firePropustio sam zadnji autobus za grad.
I missed the last bus to town.
prepustiti / prepuštatito leave (something) to someonev. pf./impf.+ dative: prepustiti odluku tebi; prepustiti se + dative = surrender oneself toOvu važnu odluku prepuštam tebi.
I leave this important decision to you.
napustiti / napuštatito abandon, leave (for good)v. pf./impf.napustiti posao/grad/obitelj, stronger and more final than otićiMnogi mladi napuštaju selo i odlaze u grad.
Many young people leave the village and go to the city.
staviti / stavljatito put, placev. pf./impf.base pair of the -staviti family; staviti knjigu na stol = put the book on the tableStavi mlijeko u hladnjak, molim te.
Put the milk in the fridge, please.
predstaviti / predstavljatito introduce, present; to representv. pf./impf.predstaviti se = introduce oneself; to predstavlja problem = that constitutes a problemDopustite da vam predstavim svog kolegu.
Allow me to introduce my colleague to you.
nastaviti / nastavljatito continuev. pf./impf.+ infinitive or s + instrumental: nastavi čitati!; noun nastava = classesNakon pauze nastavili smo s poslom.
After the break we continued with work.
ostaviti / ostavljatito leave (behind)v. pf./impf.ostaviti ključ kod susjeda; ostaviti nekoga = leave a partner; not the same as ostati = stayOstavila sam kišobran u vlaku.
I left my umbrella on the train.
sastaviti / sastavljatito put together, assemble, composev. pf./impf.sastaviti popis/rečenicu/ormar; noun sastav = essay, compositionSastavili smo popis za kupovinu.
We put together a shopping list.
postaviti / postavljatito set (up), place; to pose (a question)v. pf./impf.postaviti pitanje = ask a question; postaviti stol = set the tableSmijem li vam postaviti jedno pitanje?
May I ask you one question?
izostaviti / izostavljatito leave out, omitv. pf./impf.cf. izostati = be absent (yourself); izostaviti = leave something/someone outIzostavili su moje ime s popisa.
They left my name off the list.
pretpostaviti / pretpostavljatito assume, supposev. pf./impf.pretpostavljam da... = I suppose that...; from pred + postaviti (place before)Pretpostavljam da ćeš doći na večeru.
I assume you will come to dinner.
rastaviti / rastavljatito take apart; to separatev. pf./impf.rastaviti se = get divorced; rastaviti riječ na slogove = split a word into syllablesRastavili su stari ormar prije selidbe.
They took the old wardrobe apart before the move.
zaustaviti / zaustavljatito stop (something); (se) to come to a stopv. pf./impf.transitive: zaustaviti auto/taksi; cf. stati = stop (by yourself, intransitive)Policajac je zaustavio auto na cesti.
The policeman stopped a car on the road.

Abstract nouns & word formation B1

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
ponašanjebehaviourn. n.verbal noun in -nje from ponašati se (to behave)Njegovo ponašanje na sastanku me iznenadilo.
His behaviour at the meeting surprised me.
razmišljanjethinking, reflectionn. n.from razmišljati; način razmišljanja = way of thinkingNakon dugog razmišljanja prihvatio je posao.
After long reflection he accepted the job.
odlučnostdecisiveness, determinationn. f.-ost nouns are feminine i-declension; instr. sg. odlučnošćuNjezina odlučnost pomogla joj je u karijeri.
Her determination helped her in her career.
sposobnostability, capabilityn. f.from sposoban (capable); sposobnost + genitive or za + accusativeIma sposobnost brzog učenja jezika.
He has the ability to learn languages quickly.
sigurnostsafety, security; certaintyn. f.from siguran; sa sigurnošću = with certaintySigurnost putnika je najvažnija.
Passenger safety is the most important thing.
nesigurnostinsecurity, uncertaintyn. f.ne- negates the base noun, a productive patternPrije ispita uvijek osjećam nesigurnost.
Before an exam I always feel uncertainty.
nemogućnostimpossibilityn. f.zbog nemogućnosti + genitive = because it was impossible to...Zbog nemogućnosti dolaska otkazao je sastanak.
Because he was unable to come, he cancelled the meeting.
sličnostsimilarityn. f.sličnost između + genitive, or s + instrumentalVidim veliku sličnost između brata i sestre.
I see a great similarity between the brother and sister.
različitostdiversity, difference(s)n. f.abstract; cf. razlika = a specific differenceTrebamo poštovati različitost među ljudima.
We should respect diversity among people.
budućnostfuturen. f.u budućnosti = in the futureNitko ne zna što nosi budućnost.
Nobody knows what the future holds.
prošlostpastn. f.from prošli (last, past); u prošlosti = in the pastNe treba živjeti u prošlosti.
One shouldn't live in the past.
sadašnjostthe present (time)n. f.from sada (now); the trio prošlost (sadašnjost) budućnostVažno je uživati u sadašnjosti.
It is important to enjoy the present.
stvarnostrealityn. f.from stvaran (real); u stvarnosti = in realityNjegovi planovi su daleko od stvarnosti.
His plans are far from reality.
susretmeeting, encountern. m.from susresti (to encounter); also a sports fixtureRadujem se našem sljedećem susretu.
I am looking forward to our next meeting.
susretljivosthelpfulness, obligingnessn. f.from susretljiv, literally someone who 'meets you halfway'Hvala vam na susretljivosti i pomoći.
Thank you for your helpfulness and assistance.
poštenjehonestyn. n.from pošten (already known); cf. iskrenost = sincerityCijenim poštenje više od uspjeha.
I value honesty more than success.
strpljenjepatiencen. n.adjective strpljiv (already known); imati strpljenja s + instrumentalZa rad s djecom treba puno strpljenja.
Working with children takes a lot of patience.
hrabrostcouragen. f.from hrabar (already known)Za tu odluku treba prava hrabrost.
That decision takes real courage.
slabostweaknessn. f.imati slabost prema + dative = have a soft spot forSlatkiši su moja najveća slabost.
Sweets are my greatest weakness.
snagastrength, powern. f.nemam snage (genitive after negation) = I have no strengthNemam više snage za trčanje.
I don't have any more strength for running.
dojamimpressionn. m.fleeting a: gen. sg. dojma; ostaviti dobar dojam = make a good impressionOstavila je odličan dojam na razgovoru za posao.
She made an excellent impression at the job interview.
doživljajexperience (a single event)n. m.from doživjeti; cf. iskustvo = accumulated experienceKoncert je bio nezaboravan doživljaj.
The concert was an unforgettable experience.
uspomenamemory, keepsaken. f.uspomena na + accusative; kupiti za uspomenu = buy as a souvenirOva fotografija je uspomena s putovanja.
This photo is a keepsake from the trip.
sjećanjememory, remembrancen. n.from sjećati se; sjećanje na + accusativeSjećanje na taj dan još je živo.
The memory of that day is still vivid.
razlikadifferencen. f.razlika između + genitive; za razliku od + genitive = unlikeKoja je razlika između ova dva izraza?
What is the difference between these two expressions?
vezaconnection; relationshipn. f.biti u vezi = be in a relationship; u vezi s + instrumental = regarding; nemam veze s tim = I have nothing to do with thatOni su u vezi već tri godine.
They have been in a relationship for three years.
prijetnjathreatn. f.from prijetiti (to threaten); prijetnja + dative (a threat to something)Suša je velika prijetnja poljoprivredi.
Drought is a big threat to agriculture.
podrškasupportn. f.from podržati; pružiti podršku + dative = give support to someoneHvala ti na podršci u teškim trenucima.
Thank you for the support in difficult moments.
pomoćhelp, aidn. f.i-declension: gen. pomoći, instr. pomoću (B1 grammar point); hitna pomoć = ambulanceTrebam pomoć oko zadaće iz matematike.
I need help with my maths homework.
dogovoragreement, arrangementn. m.from dogovoriti se; po dogovoru = as agreedOstajemo pri starom dogovoru.
We are sticking to the old arrangement.
izgovorpronunciation; excusen. m.two meanings: izgovor riječi (pronunciation) vs tražiti izgovor (look for an excuse)Uvijek nađe izgovor za kašnjenje.
He always finds an excuse for being late.
govorspeechn. m.održati govor = give a speech; u govoru = in spoken languageDirektor je održao kratak govor.
The director gave a short speech.
izrazexpression, phrasen. m.izraz lica = facial expression; jezični izraz = a (set) phraseTaj izraz koristimo samo u govoru.
We use that expression only in speech.
izgledappearance, lookn. m.from izgledati; plural izgledi = prospects, chancesNe sudi ljudima po izgledu.
Don't judge people by their appearance.
radnjaplot; action; small shopn. f.radnja filma/romana = the plot; in grammar, verbs express a radnja (action)Radnja filma događa se u Dubrovniku.
The film's plot takes place in Dubrovnik.
nazivname, title (of a thing)n. m.from nazvati/nazivati; cf. ime = personal name; naziv ulice/proizvodaNe mogu se sjetiti naziva te knjige.
I can't remember the title of that book.
izazovchallengen. m.from izazvati; biti izazov za + accusativeNovi posao je velik izazov za mene.
The new job is a big challenge for me.
sadržajcontent(s)n. m.from sadržavati (to contain); sadržaj knjige = table of contentsSadržaj knjige nalazi se na početku.
The table of contents is at the beginning of the book.
nastavaclasses, instructionn. f.same root as nastaviti; na nastavi = in class; izostati s nastave = miss classNastava počinje u osam sati.
Classes start at eight o'clock.
sastavessay, composition; make-up, line-upn. m.from sastaviti; školski sastav = school essay; sastav momčadi = team line-upZa zadaću pišemo sastav o obitelji.
For homework we're writing an essay about family.

Discourse & opinion phrases B1

TermEnglishPart of speechNoteExampleCorrection / notes
tako štoby (doing something)conj.explains manner: naučio je tako što je vježbao = he learned by practisingNaučila je jezik tako što je puno čitala.
She learned the language by reading a lot.
na taj načinin that wayphr.način = way, manner; also na koji način? = in what way?Na taj način štedimo vrijeme i novac.
In that way we save time and money.
između ostalogamong other thingsphr.između + genitiveRazgovarali smo, između ostalog, o poslu.
We talked, among other things, about work.
na neki načinin a wayphr.softens a statementNa neki način ga razumijem.
In a way I understand him.
u posljednje vrijemelately, recentlyphr.used with present tense for ongoing situationsU posljednje vrijeme puno radim.
Lately I have been working a lot.
sve višemore and morephr.sve + comparative = increasingly: sve bolje, sve težeSve više ljudi radi od kuće.
More and more people work from home.
sve manjeless and lessphr.with a noun takes genitive: sve manje vremenaImamo sve manje slobodnog vremena.
We have less and less free time.
iz dana u danday by dayphr.expresses gradual changeCijene rastu iz dana u dan.
Prices are rising day by day.
s vremena na vrijemefrom time to timephr.synonym of ponekad (already known)S vremena na vrijeme odem u kazalište.
From time to time I go to the theatre.
u prosjekuon averagephr.prosjek = average; iznad/ispod prosjeka = above/below averageU prosjeku spavam sedam sati.
On average I sleep seven hours.
na temeljuon the basis ofphr.+ genitive: na temelju rezultata; temelj = foundationOdluku su donijeli na temelju rezultata.
They made the decision on the basis of the results.
s obzirom naconsidering, givenphr.+ accusative: s obzirom na kišu; also s obzirom na to da + clauseS obzirom na kišu, ostajemo kod kuće.
Given the rain, we are staying home.
u odnosu nacompared to, in relation tophr.+ accusative; odnos = relation(ship)U odnosu na prošlu godinu, cijene su više.
Compared to last year, prices are higher.
što prijeas soon as possiblephr.što + comparative = as ... as possible: što bolje, što višeJavi mi se što prije, molim te.
Get in touch as soon as possible, please.
što se mene tičeas far as I am concernedphr.ticati se + genitive = to concern; to me se ne tiče = that's none of my businessŠto se mene tiče, možemo krenuti odmah.
As far as I'm concerned, we can leave right away.
koliko znamas far as I knowphr.hedging phrase; also koliko ja znamKoliko znam, trgovina radi do osam.
As far as I know, the shop is open until eight.
ako se ne varamif I am not mistakenphr.from varati se = to be mistakenAko se ne varam, sutra je praznik.
If I'm not mistaken, tomorrow is a holiday.
i tako daljeand so onphr.abbreviated itd.Kupili smo kruh, sir, voće i tako dalje.
We bought bread, cheese, fruit and so on.
i sličnoand the like, and similarphr.abbreviated i sl.Na tečaju pišemo pisma, sastave i slično.
In the course we write letters, essays and the like.
tako rećiso to speakphr.also written takorećiOn je, tako reći, član naše obitelji.
He is, so to speak, a member of our family.
umjestoinstead ofprep.+ genitive: umjesto kave; umjesto da + clause = instead of doingUmjesto kave, danas pijem čaj.
Instead of coffee, today I am drinking tea.
čini mi seit seems to mephr.činiti se + dative; čini se da... = it seems that...Čini mi se da će padati kiša.
It seems to me that it is going to rain.

2. Grammar

A1

A1 grammar unlocks the survival core of Croatian: introducing yourself, describing people and things in the nominative, using the accusative for what you eat, buy and see, and talking about the past (perfekt) and future (futur I) with the most common verb classes.

The alphabet and sounds (abeceda i glasovi)

Croatian uses a 30-letter Latin alphabet where every letter is always pronounced the same way, so once you learn the sounds you can read anything aloud. Five letters carry diacritics: č (hard 'ch' as in 'church'), ć (soft 'ch', tongue closer to the palate), š ('sh'), ž ('s' in 'pleasure') and đ (soft 'j' as in 'jeans'). Three sounds are written with two letters but count as one: dž (hard 'j'), lj ('lli' in 'million') and nj ('ny' in 'canyon'). Stress never falls on the last syllable of a word; in most words it is on the first syllable. The letter r can act as a vowel between consonants (trg, prst, Hrvatska).

Letter  Sound (approx.)        Example
------  ---------------------  ----------------
c       ts in 'cats'           cesta (road)
č       hard ch in 'church'    čaj (tea)
ć       soft ch (palatal)      kuća (house)
dž      hard j in 'jam'        džep (pocket)
đ       soft j in 'jeans'      đak (pupil)
h       kh, as in 'loch'       hvala (thanks)
j       y in 'yes'             jutro (morning)
lj      lli in 'million'       ljeto (summer)
nj      ny in 'canyon'         knjiga (book)
š       sh in 'shoe'           škola (school)
ž       s in 'pleasure'        žena (woman)
r       can be a vowel         trg, prst, Hrvatska
  • Kako se to piše? — How is that spelled?
  • Čitam knjigu u kući. — I am reading a book in the house.
  • Hrvatski jezik ima trideset glasova. — The Croatian language has thirty sounds.
Corrections: _______________________________

Noun gender and the nominative (rod imenica i nominativ)

Every Croatian noun is masculine, feminine or neuter, and you can usually tell from the nominative singular ending: masculine nouns end in a consonant (grad, stol), feminine nouns end in -a (žena, kuća), and neuter nouns end in -o or -e (selo, more). A smaller group of feminine nouns ends in a consonant (noć, ljubav), these follow the i-declension covered later. Two sound rules affect many forms: the 'fleeting a' (nepostojano a) drops from the last syllable when an ending is added (momak → momci, pas → psi), and sibilarization changes k, g, h to c, z, s before the ending -i (momak → momci, bubreg → bubrezi). Most one-syllable masculine nouns take a long plural in -ovi/-evi (grad → gradovi, muž → muževi; -evi appears after soft consonants like č, ž, š, đ, ć, j, lj, nj).

Gender             Nom. sg.        Nom. pl.         Examples
-----------------  --------------  ---------------  -----------------------
masculine          -ø (consonant)  -i               student -> studenti
masc. (1 syllable) -ø              -ovi / -evi      grad -> gradovi
                                                    muž  -> muževi
feminine (-a)      -a              -e               žena -> žene
feminine (i-decl.) -ø (consonant)  -i               noć  -> noći
neuter             -o / -e         -a               selo -> sela
                                                    more -> mora
Sound changes in the plural
---------------------------------------------
sibilarization  k -> c   momak  -> momci
(before -i)     g -> z   bubreg -> bubrezi
                h -> s   orah   -> orasi
fleeting a      momak -> momka -> momci
(drops before   pas   -> psa   -> psi
an ending)      vrabac -> vrapca -> vrapci
  • Grad je velik, a sela su mala. — The city is big, and the villages are small.
  • Momci i djevojke plešu. — The young men and girls are dancing.
  • Muževi mojih sestara su liječnici. — My sisters' husbands are doctors.
Corrections: _______________________________

Personal pronouns and 'to be' (lične zamjenice i glagol biti)

The verb biti (to be) has three sets of present forms: long (stressed) forms used in short answers and for emphasis (Jesam!), short (clitic) forms used in normal sentences (Ja sam student), and negative forms (nisam). The short forms are enclitics, they can never stand first in a sentence; they lean on the first stressed word (Student sam). Because verb endings show the person, subject pronouns (ja, ti, on...) are normally dropped unless you want contrast or emphasis. The reflexive verb zvati se (to be called) is how you give your name: Zovem se Ana; the clitic se follows the same second-position rule.

Person        Long     Short   Negative
------------  -------  ------  --------
ja            jesam    sam     nisam
ti            jesi     si      nisi
on/ona/ono    jest     je      nije
mi            jesmo    smo     nismo
vi            jeste    ste     niste
oni/one/ona   jesu     su      nisu
zvati se (present)
------------------
ja      zovem se     mi   zovemo se
ti      zoveš se     vi   zovete se
on/ona  zove se      oni  zovu se
Word order: Zovem se Ana. / Kako se zoveš?
  • Ja sam Ivan. Drago mi je. — I am Ivan. Nice to meet you.
  • Jesi li ti student? Jesam. — Are you a student? I am.
  • Ona nije umorna. — She is not tired.
  • Zovem se Marija, a kako se vi zovete? — My name is Marija, and what is your name?
Corrections: _______________________________

The present tense: -am, -im, -em classes (prezent)

Croatian has one present tense, and every verb belongs to one of three ending classes: -am (most verbs in -ati: gledati → gledam), -im (verbs in -iti and -jeti: govoriti → govorim, živjeti → živim) and -em (verbs whose present stem differs from the infinitive: pisati → pišem, ići → idem). The endings themselves are completely regular, only the stem must be learned. Verbs in -ovati/-evati/-ivati switch to -ujem (putovati → putujem, kupovati → kupujem), while verbs in -irati stay in the -am class (studirati → studiram). A few everyday verbs are irregular and must be memorized: jesti → jedem, piti → pijem, ići → idem, slati → šaljem, pisati → pišem. Negation puts ne directly before the verb (ne radim); only imati has a fused negative, nemati (nemam).

          -am class      -im class      -em class
          gledati        govoriti       pisati
          (to watch)     (to speak)     (to write)
--------  -------------  -------------  ----------
ja        gledam         govorim        pišem
ti        gledaš         govoriš        pišeš
on/ona    gleda          govori         piše
mi        gledamo        govorimo       pišemo
vi        gledate        govorite       pišete
oni       gledaju        govore         pišu
Infinitive pattern      Present        Example
----------------------  -------------  --------------------
-ati                    -am            gledati -> gledam
-irati                  -iram          studirati -> studiram
-iti / -jeti            -im            govoriti -> govorim
                                       živjeti  -> živim
-ovati / -evati / -ivati  -ujem        putovati -> putujem
                                       kazivati -> kazujem
irregular stems         -em            jesti -> jedem
                                       piti  -> pijem
                                       ići   -> idem
                                       slati -> šaljem
  • Svaki dan gledam televiziju. — I watch television every day.
  • Govorimo hrvatski i engleski. — We speak Croatian and English.
  • Ana pije kavu i jede sendvič. — Ana is drinking coffee and eating a sandwich.
  • Nemam vremena, putujem sutra. — I have no time, I am travelling tomorrow.
Corrections: _______________________________

Numbers up to a trillion (brojevi do bilijun)

Croatian numbers are built regularly: 11-19 add -naest (jedanaest, dvanaest), tens add -deset (dvadeset, trideset), and larger units are sto (100), tisuća (1,000), milijun and bilijun. The number jedan agrees like an adjective (jedan grad, jedna žena, jedno selo), and dva has a feminine form dvije. After dva/dvije, tri and četiri, the noun takes a special paucal form identical to the genitive singular (dva grada, tri žene); after pet and higher, it takes the genitive plural (pet gradova, šest žena). This agreement rule applies to the last word of a compound number: dvadeset jedan student, dvadeset dva studenta, dvadeset pet studenata.

1 jedan/jedna/jedno   11 jedanaest    10  deset
2 dva/dvije           12 dvanaest     20  dvadeset
3 tri                 13 trinaest     30  trideset
4 četiri              14 četrnaest    40  četrdeset
5 pet                 15 petnaest     50  pedeset
6 šest                16 šesnaest     60  šezdeset
7 sedam               17 sedamnaest   70  sedamdeset
8 osam                18 osamnaest    80  osamdeset
9 devet               19 devetnaest   90  devedeset
100 sto    200 dvjesto    1 000 tisuća
1 000 000 milijun          1 000 000 000 000 bilijun

After 1          nom. sg.   jedan grad, jedna žena
After 2, 3, 4    gen. sg.   dva grada, dvije žene
After 5+         gen. pl.   pet gradova, šest žena
  • Imam trideset dvije godine. — I am thirty-two years old.
  • Kava košta dva eura, a sok tri eura. — Coffee costs two euros, and juice three euros.
  • U Zagrebu živi gotovo milijun ljudi. — Almost a million people live in Zagreb.
Corrections: _______________________________

The accusative case (akuzativ)

The accusative marks the direct object (the thing directly affected by the verb (Čitam knjigu)) and is also used after the prepositions u and na for motion toward a place (Idem u školu, Idemo na more) and after po ('to fetch') and za ('for'). Feminine nouns in -a change -a to -u (žena → ženu); neuter nouns and inanimate masculine nouns look exactly like the nominative (Vidim grad); but animate masculine nouns (people and animals) take -a, borrowing the genitive form (Vidim prijatelja). In the plural, masculine nouns take -e, feminine nouns -e, i-declension nouns -i, and neuter nouns -a.

Accusative singular
Gender             Ending      Example
-----------------  ----------  ----------------------
m. inanimate       = nom.      grad  -> Vidim grad
m. animate         -a          prijatelj -> Vidim prijatelja
f. (-a)            -u          žena  -> Vidim ženu
f. (i-declension)  = nom.      noć   -> Čekam noć
neuter             = nom.      selo  -> Vidim selo

Accusative plural
m. -e   gradove, prijatelje
f. -e   žene
f. -i   noći
n. -a   sela
Prepositions with the accusative (motion / purpose)
---------------------------------------------------
u  + A   into        Idem u grad.
na + A   onto, to    Idemo na more.
po + A   to fetch    Idem po kruh.
za + A   for         Ovo je poklon za tebe.
  • Svako jutro pijem kavu i čitam novine. — Every morning I drink coffee and read the newspaper.
  • Vidim brata i sestru. — I see my brother and sister.
  • Idemo u kino, a poslije na večeru. — We are going to the cinema, and afterwards to dinner.
  • Kupujem poklon za majku. — I am buying a present for my mother.
Corrections: _______________________________

Possessives, demonstratives and descriptive adjectives (posvojne i pokazne zamjenice, opisni pridjevi)

Possessive pronouns (moj, tvoj, njegov, njezin, naš, vaš, njihov) and descriptive adjectives agree with the noun they describe in gender and number: moj brat, moja sestra, moje selo; velik grad, velika kuća, veliko more. Croatian has a three-way demonstrative system based on distance: ovaj (near me), taj (near you), onaj (over there); their plurals are irregular, ovaj → ovi, taj → ti, onaj → oni. To say that something belongs to a person, Croatian prefers a possessive adjective made from the name or noun: -ov/-ev for masculine possessors (Markov auto, Hrvojev brat), -in for feminine (Anin stan, sestrin muž); this pattern is used for living possessors, while for inanimate things you use the genitive or a relational adjective instead (vrata kuće, gradski trg).

Possessive     m.        f.        n.
-------------  --------  --------  --------
my             moj       moja      moje
your (sg.)     tvoj      tvoja     tvoje
his            njegov    njegova   njegovo
her            njezin    njezina   njezino
our            naš       naša      naše
your (pl./V)   vaš       vaša      vaše
their          njihov    njihova   njihovo
Demonstrative   m. sg.  f. sg.  n. sg.  m. pl.  f. pl.  n. pl.
--------------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------
this (near me)  ovaj    ova     ovo     ovi     ove     ova
that (near you) taj     ta      to      ti      te      ta
that (yonder)   onaj    ona     ono     oni     one     ona
Possessive adjectives from persons
----------------------------------
masc. possessor  -ov / -ev   Marko -> Markov stan
                             Hrvoje -> Hrvojev auto
fem. possessor   -in         Ana -> Anin brat
                             sestra -> sestrin muž
  • Ovo je moja sestra, a ono je njezin muž. — This is my sister, and that over there is her husband.
  • Ovi studenti uče hrvatski, a ti studenti uče njemački. — These students are learning Croatian, and those students are learning German.
  • Markov auto je nov i brz. — Marko's car is new and fast.
Corrections: _______________________________

Modal verbs (modalni glagoli: morati, smjeti, trebati, htjeti, moći)

Modal verbs combine with an infinitive to express obligation (morati, must), permission (smjeti, may), need (trebati, need to), wish (htjeti, want) and ability (moći, can): Moram raditi, Smijem li ući? Morati, smjeti and trebati conjugate regularly (moram, smijem, trebam), but htjeti and moći are irregular: hoću, hoćeš... hoće with the fused negative neću, and mogu, možeš... mogu (note 1st sg. and 3rd pl. in -u). Infinitives end in -ti or -ći (raditi, ići, doći, reći); after a modal the infinitive never changes.

         htjeti    negative   moći
-------  --------  ---------  -------
ja       hoću      neću       mogu
ti       hoćeš     nećeš      možeš
on/ona   hoće      neće       može
mi       hoćemo    nećemo     možemo
vi       hoćete    nećete     možete
oni      hoće      neće       mogu

morati -> moram (must)     smjeti -> smijem (may)
trebati -> trebam (need)   + infinitive (-ti / -ći)
  • Moram učiti, ne mogu doći na kavu. — I have to study, I can't come for coffee.
  • Smijem li ovdje parkirati? — May I park here?
  • Hoćeš li ići s nama u kino? — Do you want to go to the cinema with us?
  • Trebam kupiti kruh i mlijeko. — I need to buy bread and milk.
Corrections: _______________________________

The past tense (perfekt)

The perfekt is the all-purpose past tense in spoken Croatian. It is formed from the present of biti (short forms: sam, si, je...) plus the active past participle, which agrees with the subject in gender and number: radio sam (a man speaking), radila sam (a woman), radili smo (we). The participle is made by replacing the infinitive -ti with -o/-la/-lo (sg.) and -li/-le/-la (pl.): raditi → radio/radila. Verbs in -ći and a few others have irregular participles that must be learned: ići → išao/išla, reći → rekao/rekla, moći → mogao/mogla. Because sam/si/je are clitics, they stand in second position (Jučer sam radio); in the negative they merge with ne and can stand first (Nisam radio). With reflexive verbs, the 3rd person singular je is dropped: On se smijao (not 'se je').

Past participle (glagolski pridjev radni)
            m.        f.        n.
----------  --------  --------  --------
singular    radio     radila    radilo
plural      radili    radile    radila

Formation: infinitive minus -ti + -o/-la/-lo/-li/-le/-la
gledati -> gledao      govoriti -> govorio
živjeti -> živio       učiti    -> učio

Irregular participles
biti  -> bio,   bila,  bilo   | bili,  bile,  bila
ići   -> išao,  išla,  išlo   | išli,  išle,  išla
reći  -> rekao, rekla, reklo  | rekli, rekle, rekla
moći  -> mogao, mogla, moglo  | mogli, mogle, mogla
perfekt = biti (short) + participle
Ja sam radio/radila.        Nisam radio/radila.
Ti si radio/radila.         Jesi li radio/radila?
On je radio. Ona je radila. On se smijao. (no 'je' with se)
Mi smo radili/radile.       Radili smo cijeli dan.
  • Jučer sam bila u Zagrebu. — Yesterday I was in Zagreb. (female speaker)
  • Gdje ste bili za vikend? — Where were you at the weekend?
  • Išli smo na more i kupali smo se. — We went to the seaside and swam.
  • Rekao je da ne može doći. — He said that he can't come.
Corrections: _______________________________

The future tense (futur prvi)

Futur I is formed with the clitic present of htjeti (ću, ćeš, će, ćemo, ćete, će) plus the infinitive. Word order determines spelling: if the infinitive comes first, verbs in -ti drop the final i and the clitic follows (Radit ću, Gledat ćemo, pronounced as one word), while verbs in -ći keep their full form (Doći ću). If anything else starts the sentence, the clitic comes second and the infinitive keeps -ti (Sutra ću raditi, Ja ću doći). The negative uses the stressed forms neću, nećeš... which can stand first (Neću raditi), and questions use Hoćeš li...? or the colloquial Hoćeš li doći? With reflexive verbs, se joins the clitic cluster: Vidjet ćemo se sutra.

Person   Clitic   Infinitive-first     Other-first
-------  -------  -------------------  ------------------
ja       ću       Radit ću.            Sutra ću raditi.
ti       ćeš      Radit ćeš.           Ti ćeš raditi.
on/ona   će       Radit će.            On će raditi.
mi       ćemo     Radit ćemo.          Mi ćemo raditi.
vi       ćete     Radit ćete.          Vi ćete raditi.
oni      će       Radit će.            Oni će raditi.

-ći verbs keep the full infinitive: Doći ću. Ići ćemo.
negative: neću, nećeš, neće, nećemo, nećete, neće + inf.
question: Hoćeš li doći? / Hoćete li raditi?
  • Sutra ću kupiti kartu za vlak. — Tomorrow I will buy a train ticket.
  • Doći ćemo u osam sati. — We will come at eight o'clock.
  • Neću raditi u nedjelju. — I will not work on Sunday.
  • Vidjet ćemo se sljedeći tjedan. — We will see each other next week.
Corrections: _______________________________

The dative and indirect objects (dativ i neizravni objekt)

The dative marks the indirect object, the person to whom something is given, said or sent: Dajem prijatelju knjigu (I give my friend a book). Singular endings: masculine and neuter -u (prijatelju, djetetu), feminine -i (ženi, sestri; with sibilarization: ruka → ruci); plural -ima/-ama for all genders. Some common verbs govern the dative directly (glagoli s dativnom rekcijom): pomagati komu (to help), vjerovati komu (to believe), telefonirati komu (to phone), čestitati komu (to congratulate), zahvaliti komu (to thank). The verb boljeti works differently, the body part is the subject and the person in pain is in the accusative: Boli me glava (my head hurts), Bole me leđa. When a sentence has both objects, the direct object is accusative and the recipient dative: Pišem baki pismo.

Dative endings
                sg.        pl.
--------------  ---------  -----------
m.              -u         -ima
                prijatelju prijateljima
n.              -u         -ima
                djetetu    djeci*
f. (-a)         -i         -ama
                ženi       ženama
f. (i-decl.)    -i         -ima
                noći       noćima
sibilarization in f. sg.: ruka -> ruci, noga -> nozi, knjiga -> knjizi

Dative-rection verbs
pomagati komu     Pomažem majci.
vjerovati komu    Vjerujem ti.
telefonirati komu Telefoniram bratu.
čestitati komu    Čestitam ti rođendan.
zahvaliti komu    Zahvaljujem vam.

boljeti: body part = subject, person = accusative
Boli me glava.  Bole me leđa.  Boli ga zub.
  • Dajem prijatelju knjigu. — I am giving my friend a book.
  • Svaki dan pomažem majci. — I help my mother every day.
  • Boli me glava, a njega bole leđa. — My head hurts, and his back hurts.
  • Čestitali smo joj rođendan. — We wished her a happy birthday.
Corrections: _______________________________

I-declension nouns and pluralia tantum (imenice i-deklinacije, pluralia tantum)

A group of feminine nouns ends in a consonant and follows the i-declension: noć, stvar, ljubav, riječ, and all abstract nouns in -ost (radost, mladost, mogućnost). Their pattern is very simple, genitive, dative and locative singular and nominative plural all end in -i (noći). Some nouns exist only in the plural (pluralia tantum) and always take plural agreement even for one object: neuter vrata (door), kola (car/cart), leđa (back), usta (mouth), and feminine hlače (trousers), naočale (glasses), novine (newspaper), škare (scissors). The noun posao (job) has an irregular stem: the -ao becomes -l- before endings (posao, posla, poslu; plural poslovi).

i-declension: noć (f.)          -ost nouns: radost (f.)
      sg.     pl.                     sg.       pl.
N     noć     noći               N    radost    radosti
G     noći    noći               G    radosti   radosti
D     noći    noćima             D    radosti   radostima
A     noć     noći               A    radost    radosti
L     noći    noćima             L    radosti   radostima
I     noći/noću  noćima          I    radošću   radostima
posao (m.): posao, posla, poslu, posao, poslu, poslom
plural:      poslovi, poslova, poslovima, poslove, ...

Pluralia tantum (always plural)
neuter:   vrata (door), kola (car), leđa (back), usta (mouth)
feminine: hlače (trousers), naočale (glasses),
          novine (newspaper), škare (scissors)
Vrata su otvorena.  Hlače su nove.
  • Noći su ljeti kratke. — In summer the nights are short.
  • Imam puno posla ove noći. — I have a lot of work tonight.
  • Vrata su zatvorena, a novine su na stolu. — The door is closed, and the newspaper is on the table.
  • Mladost brzo prolazi. — Youth passes quickly.
Corrections: _______________________________

Imperative basics (imperativ glagola na -iti, -ati)

The imperative gives commands and instructions and has forms for ti, mi and vi. It is built from the 3rd person plural present: if that form ends in -aju, the imperative ending is -aj (gledaju → gledaj!, gledajte!); if it ends in -e or -u after a consonant, the ending is -i (govore → govori!, govorite!; uče → uči!). The vi-form doubles as the polite form for one person (Izvolite, uđite!). The negative imperative uses nemoj/nemojte + infinitive for polite prohibition (Nemoj kasniti!) or ne + imperative (Ne kasni!).

         gledati (-ati)   govoriti (-iti)
-------  ---------------  ----------------
(ti)     gledaj!          govori!
(mi)     gledajmo!        govorimo!
(vi)     gledajte!        govorite!

Rule: from 3rd pl. present
-aju -> -aj(te)    gledaju -> gledaj!
-e/-u -> -i(te)    govore  -> govori!  pišu -> piši!

negative: nemoj + inf. / ne + imperative
Nemoj kasniti! = Ne kasni!
  • Govori sporije, molim te! — Speak more slowly, please!
  • Gledajte ovu fotografiju. — Look at this photograph. (polite/plural)
  • Nemojte zaboraviti putovnicu. — Don't forget your passport. (polite/plural)
Corrections: _______________________________

A2

A2 grammar completes the case system (full declension of nouns, adjectives and pronouns in all seven cases) and adds comparison, the conditional, verbal aspect and the clitic-order rules you need for natural, correctly built sentences.

Full noun declension: the three classes (sklonidba imenica)

Croatian nouns decline through seven cases (nominative, genitive, dative, accusative, vocative, locative, instrumental) in singular and plural, and every noun follows one of three patterns: the a-declension (masculine and neuter: grad, prijatelj, selo), the e-declension (nouns in -a, mostly feminine: žena) and the i-declension (feminine nouns in a consonant: noć). Dative and locative are always identical, and in the plural dative, locative and instrumental share one form (-ima/-ama). Masculine instrumental singular is -om after hard consonants and -em after soft ones (č, ć, đ, ž, š, j, lj, nj: prijateljem, mužem). Animate masculine nouns take the genitive form in the accusative singular (Vidim prijatelja), while inanimate ones match the nominative.

a-declension, masculine
     grad (inanimate)         prijatelj (animate, soft)
     sg.       pl.            sg.          pl.
N    grad      gradovi        prijatelj    prijatelji
G    grada     gradova        prijatelja   prijatelja
D    gradu     gradovima      prijatelju   prijateljima
A    grad      gradove        prijatelja   prijatelje
V    grade     gradovi        prijatelju   prijatelji
L    gradu     gradovima      prijatelju   prijateljima
I    gradom    gradovima      prijateljem  prijateljima
e-declension: žena (f.)      a-declension, neuter: selo
     sg.      pl.                sg.      pl.
N    žena     žene           N   selo     sela
G    žene     žena           G   sela     sela
D    ženi     ženama         D   selu     selima
A    ženu     žene           A   selo     sela
V    ženo     žene           V   selo     sela
L    ženi     ženama         L   selu     selima
I    ženom    ženama         I   selom    selima
i-declension: noć (f.)
     sg.        pl.
N    noć        noći
G    noći       noći
D    noći       noćima
A    noć        noći
V    noći       noći
L    noći       noćima
I    noći/noću  noćima
  • Vraćam se iz grada u selo. — I am returning from the city to the village.
  • Razgovarao sam s prijateljem o ženama i poslu. — I talked with a friend about women and work.
  • U velikim gradovima ima puno automobila. — In big cities there are lots of cars.
