Special noun patterns: stem extensions, foreign nouns, dio (posebne sklonidbe)

Some neuter nouns extend their stem outside the nominative/accusative singular with -(e)n- or -(e)t-: ime → imena (G sg.), rame → ramena; dijete → djeteta, tele → teleta (and the plural of dijete is the collective djeca). Foreign nouns ending in -y, -i, -u, -o, -e decline like masculine nouns by inserting -j- or adding endings to the full form: taksi → taksija, intervju → intervjua, auto → auta, finale → finala; nouns in -io insert -j-: radio → radija, studio → studija. The noun dio (part) changes its stem to dijel-: dio, dijela, dijelu, plural dijelovi, the same -io → -jel- alternation as posao → posla.

Stem extension -(e)n- / -(e)t- (neuter)
      ime (name)        dijete (child)
N sg  ime               dijete
G sg  imena             djeteta
D sg  imenu             djetetu
I sg  imenom            djetetom
N pl  imena             djeca (collective!)

Foreign nouns (decline as masculine)
taksi    -> taksija, taksiju, taksijem
intervju -> intervjua, intervjuu
auto     -> auta, autu, autom
radio    -> radija, radiju, radijem
finale   -> finala, finalu

dio (part): dio, dijela, dijelu, dio, dijelu, dijelom
plural: dijelovi, dijelova, dijelovima
  • Kako se piše vaše ime i prezime? — How do you spell your first and last name?
  • Zvao sam taksi jer je auto na servisu. — I called a taxi because the car is being serviced.
  • Pročitao sam samo dio intervjua. — I read only part of the interview.
Corrections: _______________________________

Adjective declension (sklonidba pridjeva)

Adjectives agree with their noun in gender, number and case, so they decline too. Masculine and neuter share most endings (-og(a) in genitive, -om(u/e) in dative and locative, -im in instrumental), while feminine follows the e-declension pattern (-e, -oj, -u, -om). In the masculine accusative singular the animacy rule applies: inanimate matches the nominative (Vidim velik grad), animate matches the genitive (Vidim dobrog prijatelja). Adjectives like dobar show the fleeting a (dobar → dobrog). Croatian also distinguishes indefinite (dobar čovjek) and definite (dobri čovjek) masculine nominative forms, the definite form in -i is used with known referents and always after demonstratives (taj dobri čovjek). Relational adjectives in -ski, -ški, -čki, -ćki (gradski, zagrebački) describe type or origin, only have the definite form, and never form comparatives.

dobar (good), singular
Case  m.                      n.          f.
----  ----------------------  ----------  --------
N     dobar / dobri           dobro       dobra
A     = N (inanim.)           dobro       dobru
      dobrog(a) (anim.)
G     dobrog(a)               dobrog(a)   dobre
D     dobrom(u)               dobrom(u)   dobroj
L     dobrom(e)               dobrom(e)   dobroj
I     dobrim                  dobrim      dobrom

plural (all cases follow the same logic)
N  dobri (m.) dobra (n.) dobre (f.)
G  dobrih     D/L/I dobrim(a)   A dobre/dobra/dobre
Relational adjectives -ski/-ški/-čki/-ćki
grad    -> gradski trg       (city square)
Zagreb  -> zagrebački kolodvor
turist  -> turistička agencija
mladić  -> mladićki? no -> mladenački; učenik -> učenički
Always definite; no comparative.
  • Vidim dobrog prijatelja u novom autu. — I see a good friend in a new car.
  • Živim u malom stanu blizu glavnoga trga. — I live in a small flat near the main square.
  • Zagrebačke ulice su pune turista. — Zagreb's streets are full of tourists.
Corrections: _______________________________

Demonstratives, possessives and reflexive svoj in all cases (sklonidba zamjenica; povratno-posvojna zamjenica)

Demonstrative (ovaj, taj, onaj) and possessive (moj, tvoj, naš...) pronouns decline like definite adjectives: taj → tog(a), tom(u), tim; moj → mog(a)/mojeg(a), mom(u)/mojem(u), mojim. The reflexive-possessive pronoun svoj means 'one's own' and must be used whenever the possessor is the subject of the clause, regardless of person: Čitam svoju knjigu (my own), On čita svoju knjigu (his own). Using moj or njegov instead changes or blurs the meaning, Njegov auto is someone else's car, svoj auto is the subject's own. Svoj declines exactly like moj and is never used in the nominative describing the subject itself.

taj (that), singular            moj / svoj, masculine sg.
Case  m.        n.     f.        Case  form
----  --------  -----  ----      ----  -----------------
N     taj       to     ta        N     moj / svoj
G     tog(a)    tog(a) te        G     mog(a) / svog(a)
D     tom(u)    tom(u) toj       D     mom(u) / svom(u)
A     =N/G      to     tu        A     = N (inanim.) / G (anim.)
L     tom(e)    tom(e) toj       L     mom(e) / svom(e)
I     tim       tim    tom       I     mojim / svojim
(f.: svoja -> svoje, svojoj, svoju, svojoj, svojom)
svoj vs. moj/njegov
subject = possessor  -> svoj
Ja čitam svoju knjigu.   (my own book)
On vozi svoj auto.       (his own car)
subject != possessor -> moj/tvoj/njegov...
On vozi njegov auto.     (someone else's car)
  • Uzmi svoje stvari i dođi u taj kafić. — Take your things and come to that café.
  • Ana je izgubila svoj mobitel, a našla je njegov. — Ana lost her own mobile phone, and found his.
  • Razgovarali smo o tom problemu sa svojim profesorom. — We talked about that problem with our professor.
Corrections: _______________________________

Personal pronouns in all cases and clitic order (lične zamjenice; redoslijed enklitika)

Personal pronouns have stressed (naglašeni) and clitic (nenaglašeni) forms in the genitive, dative and accusative: mene/me, meni/mi, njega/ga, njoj/joj. Clitics are the default; stressed forms are used after prepositions, for contrast, and at the start of an answer (Koga vidiš? Njega.). All clitics gather in second position in the clause, in a fixed internal order: the question particle li, then verbal auxiliaries (sam, si, smo, ste, su; ću, ćeš...; bih, bi...), then the dative clitic, then the accusative/genitive clitic, then se, and the auxiliary je always comes last of all. Example: Dala mi ga je (She gave it to me). This order never varies, so it is worth memorizing as a template.

Personal pronouns: stressed / clitic
        G            D            A
ja      mene/me      meni/mi      mene/me
ti      tebe/te      tebi/ti      tebe/te
on/ono  njega/ga     njemu/mu     njega/ga
ona     nje/je       njoj/joj     nju/ju (je)
mi      nas/nas      nama/nam     nas/nas
vi      vas/vas      vama/vam     vas/vas
oni     njih/ih      njima/im     njih/ih
(after prepositions: stressed form  -> kod mene, za njega)
Clitic order template (2nd position in clause)
 li -> aux -> DAT -> ACC/GEN -> se -> je
(1)   (2)    (3)      (4)     (5)   (6)

Jesi li mu ga dao?        li + DAT + ACC
Dala mi ga je.            DAT + ACC + je last
Sjećam ga se.             GEN + se
Predstavit ću ti je.      aux + DAT + ACC
Ona mu se nasmijala.      DAT + se ('je' dropped with se)
  • Dala mi ga je jučer. — She gave it to me yesterday.
  • Jesi li ih vidio u gradu? — Did you see them in town?
  • Čekam te ispred kina, mene nemoj čekati. — I'm waiting for you in front of the cinema, don't wait for me.
  • Sjećam je se vrlo dobro. — I remember her very well.
Corrections: _______________________________

More present-tense classes (prezentske vrste)

A2 adds the remaining common present-stem patterns, all still using the regular -em endings. Verbs in -nuti conjugate with -nem (krenuti → krenem); doći and its family give dođem, dođeš. Many verbs in -ati soften their final consonant before -jem endings (iotation): pisati → pišem, kazati → kažem, plakati → plačem. Short vowel-stem verbs like čuti simply insert j (čujem, pijem), and verbs in -vati switch to -jem (davati → dajem, poznavati → poznajem). Consonant-stem verbs include the peći type (pečem, but 3rd pl. peku) and the -sti → -dem type (jesti → jedem, krasti → kradem). The stem must be learned with each verb, but once you know the 1st person singular, the whole paradigm follows automatically.

Pattern            Model        Present (ja, ti, ... oni)
-----------------  -----------  --------------------------------
-(n)uti -> -nem    krenuti      krenem, kreneš, krene,
                                krenemo, krenete, krenu
doći    -> dođem   doći         dođem, dođeš ... dođu
-ati -> -jem       pisati       pišem, pišeš ... pišu
(iotation)         kazati       kažem ... kažu
                   plakati      plačem ... plaču
čuti type          čuti         čujem, čuješ ... čuju
-vati -> -jem      davati       dajem, daješ ... daju
                   poznavati    poznajem ... poznaju
peći type          peći         pečem, pečeš ... peku (3. pl!)
-sti -> -dem       jesti        jedem, jedeš ... jedu
                   krasti       kradem ... kradu
  • Krećem na posao u sedam, a dođem kući u pet. — I leave for work at seven, and I get home at five.
  • Baka peče kolače i daje ih djeci. — Grandma bakes cakes and gives them to the children.
  • Čujem da dobro poznaješ Split. — I hear that you know Split well.
Corrections: _______________________________

Verbal aspect: perfective and imperfective (glagolski vid)

Almost every Croatian verb comes in a pair: an imperfective verb (nesvršeni) for ongoing, repeated or unfinished actions, and a perfective verb (svršeni) for single completed actions, pisati/napisati, kupovati/kupiti, dolaziti/doći. English hides this distinction in tenses ('was writing' vs 'wrote'); Croatian builds it into the verb itself, so choosing the right member of the pair matters in every tense. Perfective verbs cannot form a true present with present meaning, Napišem pismo only works in dependent clauses or with future reference; for 'I am writing' you must say Pišem. In the perfekt, aspect distinguishes Pisao sam pismo (I was writing / used to write) from Napisao sam pismo (I finished writing it). Dictionaries list verbs as pairs, and it is best to learn them together from the start.

Imperfective (process)     Perfective (completed)
-------------------------  ----------------------
pisati    (be writing)     napisati  (write, finish)
čitati    (be reading)     pročitati (read through)
kupovati  (be buying)      kupiti    (buy)
dolaziti  (be coming)      doći      (come, arrive)
gledati   (be watching)    pogledati (take a look)
učiti     (study)          naučiti   (learn, master)

Use imperfective for:  process, habit, duration
  Svaki dan pišem mailove.  Pisao sam cijelo jutro.
Use perfective for:    one whole completed event
  Napisao sam mail i poslao ga.
  • Dugo sam učio hrvatski i napokon sam naučio padeže. — I studied Croatian for a long time and finally learned the cases.
  • Kupovala je namirnice svaki dan, a jučer je kupila i vino. — She used to buy groceries every day, and yesterday she also bought wine.
  • Dolazim! Doći ću za pet minuta. — I'm coming! I'll arrive in five minutes.
Corrections: _______________________________

Comparative and superlative (komparativ i superlativ)

Most adjectives form the comparative with -iji (star → stariji, pametan → pametniji). Shorter adjectives take -ji, which fuses with the final consonant (iotation): mlad → mlađi, jak → jači, skup → skuplji, tih → tiši. Exactly three adjectives take -ši: lijep → ljepši, lak → lakši, mek → mekši. Four key adjectives are suppletive and must be memorized: dobar → bolji, loš → gori, velik → veći, malen/mali → manji. The superlative is always naj- + comparative (najbolji, najstariji). Comparatives and superlatives decline like definite adjectives (boljeg, boljem, s boljim). Comparison uses od + genitive or nego: Ivan je stariji od Marka / stariji nego Marko. Adverbs compare with the neuter form: dobro → bolje → najbolje, mnogo → više, malo → manje, loše → gore.

Pattern       Positive   Comparative   Superlative
------------  ---------  ------------  ------------
-iji          star       stariji       najstariji
              pametan    pametniji     najpametniji
-ji (iotation) mlad      mlađi         najmlađi
              jak        jači          najjači
              skup       skuplji       najskuplji
              tih        tiši          najtiši
-ši (only 3)  lijep      ljepši        najljepši
              lak        lakši         najlakši
              mek        mekši         najmekši
irregular     dobar      bolji         najbolji
              loš        gori          najgori
              velik      veći          najveći
              mali       manji         najmanji

Adverbs: dobro->bolje  loše->gore  mnogo->više  malo->manje
Than: od + G (stariji od brata) / nego (stariji nego brat)
  • Moj stan je manji od tvoga, ali je jeftiniji. — My flat is smaller than yours, but it is cheaper.
  • Ovo je najljepši grad na svijetu. — This is the most beautiful city in the world.
  • Danas se osjećam bolje nego jučer. — Today I feel better than yesterday.
Corrections: _______________________________

The conditional (kondicional prvi)

Kondicional I is formed with the aorist of biti (bih, bi, bi, bismo, biste, bi) plus the past participle: Rado bih došao (I would gladly come). These auxiliary forms are clitics and stand in second position; in careful standard Croatian the persons are distinguished (bismo, biste), even though colloquial speech levels them all to bi. The negative puts ne before the auxiliary (ne bih rekao) and the question uses inversion with li (Biste li htjeli kavu?). The conditional expresses wishes (Htio bih...), polite requests (Biste li mi pomogli?), possibility, and conditions (both realizable and unrealizable) often introduced by kad or da: Kad bih imao vremena, putovao bih.

Person   Aux.    Example
-------  ------  ---------------------------
ja       bih     Ja bih došao. / Došao bih.
ti       bi      Ti bi došao.
on/ona   bi      On bi došao.
mi       bismo   Mi bismo došli.
vi       biste   Vi biste došli.
oni      bi      Oni bi došli.

negative:  Ne bih to rekao.
question:  Bi li došao?  Biste li htjeli kavu?
meanings:  wish        Htjela bih sladoled.
           politeness  Biste li mi pomogli?
           possibility To bi moglo biti točno.
           condition   Kad bih imao novca, kupio bih stan.
  • Htio bih rezervirati stol za dvoje. — I would like to reserve a table for two.
  • Biste li mi mogli pomoći? — Could you help me? (polite)
  • Kad bih imao više vremena, učio bih hrvatski svaki dan. — If I had more time, I would study Croatian every day.
Corrections: _______________________________

Futur II and time/condition clauses (futur drugi; zavisne rečenice s kad, ako, dok)

Futur II is formed with budem, budeš, bude, budemo, budete, budu plus the past participle (budem radio). It never stands alone: it appears in dependent clauses after kad (when), ako (if) and dok (while/until) to mark a future action that precedes or accompanies the main future action: Kad budem imao vremena, nazvat ću te. With perfective verbs, the bare present usually replaces futur II in these clauses (Kad dođem, javit ću ti se), that is the normal, most frequent pattern; futur II is chiefly needed with imperfective verbs. The main clause keeps futur I. Note the meaning of dok ne + perfective: 'until' (Čekat ću dok ne dođeš).

futur II = budem + participle
ja  budem radio/radila    mi  budemo radili/radile
ti  budeš radio/radila    vi  budete radili/radile
on  bude radio            oni budu radili

Dependent clause (kad/ako/dok)     Main clause (futur I)
--------------------------------   ---------------------
Kad budem imao vremena,            nazvat ću te.
Ako budeš učio,                    položit ćeš ispit.
Dok budeš spavao,                  ja ću raditi.
perfective verb -> present instead of futur II:
Kad dođem kući,                    javit ću ti se.
Ako vidiš Anu,                     pozdravi je.
  • Ako budeš imao problema, nazovi me. — If you have problems, call me.
  • Kad budem govorio hrvatski bolje, tražit ću posao u Zagrebu. — When I speak Croatian better, I will look for a job in Zagreb.
  • Čekat ću ovdje dok ne dođeš. — I will wait here until you come.
Corrections: _______________________________

Uses of the genitive (vremenski, posvojni i objasnidbeni genitiv)

Beyond 'of' and quantities, A2 focuses on three genitive functions. The temporal genitive puts time expressions directly into the genitive with no preposition: prošle godine (last year), svakog dana (every day), jednog jutra (one morning). The possessive genitive expresses belonging when a possessive adjective is impossible, typically when the possessor carries a modifier: auto moga brata (my brother's car), kuća stare gospođe. The explanatory (objasnidbeni) genitive specifies what something consists of or refers to: osjećaj sreće (a feeling of happiness), problem nezaposlenosti, miris mora. The genitive is also required after quantity words (puno, malo, nekoliko + G pl.) and many prepositions (iz, od, do, kod, bez, blizu, pored).

Temporal G     prošle godine      last year
(no prep.)     svakog dana        every day
               ovog tjedna        this week
               jednog jutra       one morning
Possessive G   auto moga brata    my brother's car
(modified      stan naših susjeda our neighbours' flat
 possessor)
Explanatory G  osjećaj sreće      feeling of happiness
               miris mora         smell of the sea
               problem nezaposlenosti
Quantity + G   puno posla, malo vremena, nekoliko knjiga
Prepositions   iz, od, do, kod, bez, blizu, pored, ispred + G
  • Prošle godine bili smo kod mojih roditelja. — Last year we were at my parents' place.
  • To je bicikl moga mlađeg brata. — That is my younger brother's bicycle.
  • Volim miris mora i zvuk valova. — I love the smell of the sea and the sound of the waves.
Corrections: _______________________________

Impersonal sentences (impersonalne rečenice)

Croatian often builds sentences without a nominative subject. With states and feelings, the verb or adjective stands in the neuter 3rd person singular and the person appears in the dative: Hladno mi je (I am cold), Dosadno joj je (she is bored). Necessity and possibility use treba and može with an infinitive or a se-construction: Treba učiti (one must study), Može se ući (one may enter), Ovdje se ne puši (no smoking here). Past tense of all these takes the neuter singular: Bilo je hladno, Trebalo je raditi. These patterns are extremely common in everyday speech and signs, and English 'it/one/you' subjects all map onto them.

Pattern                 Example              English
----------------------  -------------------  -------------------
adj. (n.) + je + DAT    Hladno mi je.        I am cold.
                        Dosadno joj je.      She is bored.
treba + inf.            Treba puno raditi.   One must work a lot.
može se + inf./verb-se  Može se ući.         One may enter.
                        Ovdje se ne puši.    No smoking here.
past: neuter sg.        Bilo je hladno.      It was cold.
                        Trebalo je učiti.    One had to study.
  • Hladno mi je, zatvori prozor, molim te. — I'm cold, close the window, please.
  • U knjižnici se ne smije glasno govoriti. — One must not speak loudly in the library.
  • Jučer je bilo vruće, a danas je ugodno. — Yesterday it was hot, and today it is pleasant.
Corrections: _______________________________

Comparing adverbs (komparativ i superlativ priloga)

Adverbs of manner look like the neuter singular of the adjective (brzo, dobro, loše) and compare using the neuter comparative form: brzo → brže, često → češće, dobro → bolje, loše → gore, mnogo → više, malo → manje. The superlative again adds naj- (najbrže, najbolje). These comparative adverbs are everywhere in everyday speech (govori sporije (speak more slowly), dođi ranije (come earlier)) and also combine with što to mean 'as ... as possible': što prije (as soon as possible), što više (as much as possible).

Adverb     Comparative   Superlative
---------  ------------  -----------
brzo       brže          najbrže
sporo      sporije       najsporije
dobro      bolje         najbolje
loše       gore          najgore
mnogo      više          najviše
malo       manje         najmanje
često      češće         najčešće
rano       ranije        najranije
kasno      kasnije       najkasnije
što + comparative = as ... as possible
što prije (asap), što više (as much as possible)
  • Molim vas, govorite sporije. — Please speak more slowly.
  • Dođi što ranije, imamo puno posla. — Come as early as possible, we have a lot of work.
  • Najviše volim putovati ljeti. — I like travelling most in summer.
Corrections: _______________________________

B1

B1 grammar turns correct sentences into fluent Croatian: mastering aspect pairs and prefixed verb families, the passive participle, verbal nouns and adverbs, and the full range of conditional sentences lets you narrate, argue and write connected texts.

Aspect pairs in depth (vidski parovi)

At B1 you systematize how aspect pairs are formed. Three patterns cover nearly all verbs: (1) a prefix turns an imperfective into a perfective (pisati → napisati, gledati → pogledati); (2) a suffix, usually -avati, -ivati or -ati, derives a new imperfective from a perfective (kupiti → kupovati, dati → davati, dogovoriti se → dogovarati se); (3) a few pairs use different stems altogether (suppletive: dolaziti/doći, govoriti/reći, uzimati/uzeti). Crucially, when a prefix adds a new meaning (pisati → opisati 'describe'), that new perfective verb gets its own derived imperfective (opisivati), creating a secondary pair. Learning verbs in these families, rather than one by one, is the fastest route to B1 vocabulary.

Pattern                    impf.           pf.
-------------------------  --------------  --------------
1. prefix (impf. -> pf.)   pisati          napisati
   (same meaning,          čitati          pročitati
    completed)             gledati         pogledati
                           raditi          uraditi
2. suffix (pf. -> impf.)   kupiti          kupovati
   -avati/-ivati/-ati      dati            davati
                           dogovoriti se   dogovarati se
                           ostaviti        ostavljati
3. suppletive /            dolaziti        doći
   stem change             govoriti        reći
                           uzimati         uzeti

New meaning -> secondary pair:
pisati -> opisati (describe) -> opisivati (impf.)
       -> zapisati (note down) -> zapisivati (impf.)
  • Pisao sam izvještaj cijeli dan i napokon sam ga napisao. — I was writing the report all day and finally finished writing it.
  • Uzimam lijekove svaki dan; danas sam ih već uzeo. — I take medicine every day; today I have already taken it.
  • Dogovarali smo se tjednima i na kraju smo se dogovorili. — We negotiated for weeks and in the end we reached an agreement.
Corrections: _______________________________

Verb families with prefixes (glagoli u kontekstu: pisati, gledati, staviti...)

Croatian prefixes work like English phrasal-verb particles: each prefix adds a predictable shade of meaning to a base verb. From pisati: opisati (describe), zapisati (note down), potpisati (sign), prepisati (copy); from gledati: pogledati (take a look), pregledati (examine), razgledati (sightsee); from staviti: dostaviti (deliver), predstaviti (introduce), nastaviti (continue), ostaviti (leave behind), sastaviti (assemble), postaviti (set up); from stati: postati (become), ostati (stay), prestati (stop), ustati (get up). Common prefix meanings: po- (a little / begin), pre- (across, over, re-), raz- (apart, around), za- (start / fix in place), do- (reach, arrive), iz- (out), na- (onto / completion), pri- (near, join), od- (away). Learning the prefix meanings lets you decode hundreds of new verbs from context.

Base       + prefix     Meaning
---------  -----------  -----------------------
pisati     opisati      describe
(write)    zapisati     note down
           potpisati    sign
           prepisati    copy / prescribe
gledati    pogledati    take a look
(watch)    pregledati   examine, review
           razgledati   look around, sightsee
misliti    pomisliti    think of (suddenly)
(think)    izmisliti    invent, make up
           razmisliti   think over
staviti    dostaviti    deliver
(put)      predstaviti  introduce, present
           nastaviti    continue
           ostaviti     leave behind
           sastaviti    assemble, compose
           postaviti    set up, install
stati      postati      become
(stop/     ostati       stay, remain
 stand)    prestati     stop (doing)
           ustati       get up
zvati      nazvati      call (phone)
(call)     pozvati      invite
           izazvati     provoke, cause
držati     zadržati     keep, retain
(hold)     održati      hold (an event), maintain
           podržati     support
živjeti    doživjeti    experience
(live)     preživjeti   survive
pustiti    dopustiti    allow
(let)      otpustiti    dismiss, release
  • Molim vas, potpišite ugovor i zapišite datum. — Please sign the contract and note down the date.
  • Liječnik me pregledao i sve mi je objasnio. — The doctor examined me and explained everything to me.
  • Prestao je pušiti i postao je puno zdraviji. — He stopped smoking and became much healthier.
  • Dopustite da vam predstavim svoju kolegicu. — Allow me to introduce my colleague to you.
Corrections: _______________________________

Advanced present-stem classes (prezent glagola tipa stanem, sjednem, donesem)

B1 completes the present-stem system with the last consonant-stem patterns, all with regular -em endings. Verbs like ostati and postati form -anem (ostanem, postanem); uzeti and početi have suppletive stems uzmem and počnem. Verbs in -sti split into three types: -dnem (sjesti → sjednem, pasti → padnem), -tnem (sresti → sretnem) and -zem (gristi → grizem, vesti → vezem). Verbs in -ći of the stići type give -gnem (stignem, legnem, pobjegnem), and the -nijeti family gives -nesem (donijeti → donesem, odnijeti → odnesem). These are all perfective or mixed-aspect everyday verbs, so their present forms mostly appear in dependent clauses and futures (Kad stignem, sjednem i počnem raditi).

Pattern            Infinitive   Present (ja)
-----------------  -----------  ------------
-ati  -> -anem     ostati       ostanem
                   postati      postanem
suppletive         uzeti        uzmem
                   početi       počnem
-sti  -> -dnem     sjesti       sjednem
                   pasti        padnem
-sti  -> -tnem     sresti       sretnem
-sti  -> -zem      gristi       grizem
                   vesti        vezem
-ći   -> -gnem     stići        stignem
                   leći         legnem
                   pobjeći      pobjegnem
-ijeti -> -esem    donijeti     donesem
                   odnijeti     odnesem
                   ponijeti     ponesem
  • Kad stignem kući, sjednem i počnem kuhati. — When I get home, I sit down and start cooking.
  • Uzmi kišobran da ne pokisneš. — Take an umbrella so you don't get soaked.
  • Donijet ću ti knjigu čim je pročitam. — I'll bring you the book as soon as I read it.
Corrections: _______________________________

The dative of the experiencer (nositelj stanja u dativu)

Croatian systematically puts the person who experiences a state in the dative while the grammatical subject is the thing or the state itself: Sviđa mi se ovaj film (literally 'this film pleases to-me'), Hladno mi je, Dosadno nam je, Žao mi je (I'm sorry), Drago mi je (pleased to meet you). The verb agrees with the nominative subject, not with the experiencer: Sviđaju mi se ove pjesme (plural verb, plural subject). This pattern also covers physical states (Zlo mi je, I feel sick, Vrti mi se, I'm dizzy) and needs (Treba mi pomoć, I need help, Nedostaje mi obitelj, I miss my family). Getting these right is a hallmark of natural Croatian, because English speakers instinctively make the experiencer the subject.

Croatian (DAT experiencer)   Literal            English
---------------------------  -----------------  -----------------
Sviđa mi se film.            pleases to-me      I like the film.
Sviđaju mi se filmovi.       (verb agrees       I like the films.
                              with subject!)
Žao mi je.                   sorry to-me        I am sorry.
Drago mi je.                 dear to-me         Pleased to meet you.
Zlo mi je.                   ill to-me          I feel sick.
Vrti mi se.                  spins to-me        I am dizzy.
Treba mi pomoć.              is-needed to-me    I need help.
Nedostaje mi obitelj.        lacks to-me        I miss my family.
Uspjelo nam je.              succeeded to-us    We succeeded.
  • Sviđaju mi se ove pjesme, a njemu se ne sviđaju. — I like these songs, but he doesn't like them.
  • Nedostaju mi more i sunce. — I miss the sea and the sun.
  • Žao nam je što ne možete doći. — We are sorry that you can't come.
Corrections: _______________________________

Instrumental of consonant-final feminine nouns; dob and doba (instrumental i-deklinacije; imenice dob i doba)

Feminine i-declension nouns have two instrumental singular options: the ending -i (identical to the genitive/dative) or the fused ending -ju, which triggers sound changes at the stem boundary: sol → solju, ljubav → ljubavlju, misao → mišlju, radost → radošću, noć → noći/noću. The -ju forms are preferred when the noun stands alone without an adjective (Piše kredom i ljubavlju); with a modifier, -i is common (s velikom radosti/radošću). Two look-alike nouns must be kept apart: dob (age) is feminine i-declension (u mojoj dobi, at my age), while doba (period, season) is neuter and keeps the same form in all singular cases (u to doba, at that time, godišnje doba, season).

Instrumental sg. of i-declension (f.)
Noun      I sg. (-ju)      Sound change
--------  ---------------  -------------
sol       solju            l + j
ljubav    ljubavlju        v -> vlj
krv       krvlju           v -> vlj
misao     mišlju           sao -> šlj
radost    radošću          st -> šć
noć       noću / noći      -
stvar     stvarju / stvari -

dob (f., i-decl.)          doba (n., unchanged in sg.)
N dob    u mojoj dobi (L)  N/G/D/A/L doba
G dobi                     godišnje doba (season)
                           u to doba (at that time)
  • Pismo je napisano ljubavlju. — The letter was written with love.
  • Radim noću, a spavam danju. — I work at night and sleep during the day.
  • U mojoj dobi ljudi obično već imaju obitelj. — At my age people usually already have a family.
  • Zima je moje omiljeno godišnje doba. — Winter is my favourite season.
Corrections: _______________________________

Collective nouns (zbirne imenice)

Collective nouns name a group as a single mass: djeca (children), braća (brothers), gospoda (gentlemen), lišće (leaves), cvijeće (flowers), granje (branches), telad (calves), unučad (grandchildren). Grammatically they behave in a mixed way that must be learned: djeca, braća and gospoda decline like singular feminine nouns in -a (s djecom, o braći) but take a plural verb, with the participle in -la: Djeca su se igrala, Braća su došla. The -je collectives (lišće, cvijeće) are neuter singular in every respect: Lišće je palo. The -ad collectives (telad, unučad) are feminine i-declension singular: S teladi. Collectives replace the plural of some nouns entirely, dijete has no plural *dijeteta; its plural is djeca; brat's everyday plural is braća.

Collective   Meaning        Declension       Verb agreement
-----------  -------------  ---------------  -----------------
djeca        children       like žena (sg.)  plural: Djeca su
                            s djecom, djeci  se igrala.
braća        brothers       like žena (sg.)  plural: Braća su
                            s braćom, braći  došla.
gospoda      gentlemen      like žena (sg.)  plural
lišće        leaves         neuter sg.       singular: Lišće
cvijeće      flowers        neuter sg.       je palo.
granje       branches       neuter sg.       singular
telad        calves         f. i-decl. sg.   singular
unučad       grandchildren  f. i-decl. sg.   singular

dijete (sg.) -> djeca (pl.)   brat (sg.) -> braća (pl.)
  • Djeca su se cijeli dan igrala u parku. — The children played in the park all day.
  • Moja braća žive u Splitu; često razgovaram s braćom. — My brothers live in Split; I often talk with my brothers.
  • U jesen lišće mijenja boju i pada. — In autumn the leaves change colour and fall.
Corrections: _______________________________

The passive participle (glagolski pridjev trpni)

The passive participle turns a verb into an adjective meaning 'having been X-ed' and is the key to passive sentences and countless everyday expressions (zatvoreno, rezervirano, zabranjeno). Formation follows the infinitive class: verbs in -ati take -an (napisati → napisan, pročitati → pročitan); verbs in -iti and -jeti take -en with iotation of the stem consonant (učiniti → učinjen, vidjeti → viđen, baciti → bačen); consonant-stem verbs also take -en (peći → pečen, donijeti → donesen); and a small group takes -t (uzeti → uzet, početi → počet, čuti → čut, otvoriti → otvoren but zauzeti → zauzet). The participle agrees like an adjective (pečen, pečena, pečeno) and combines with biti for the passive: Ručak je skuhan (lunch is cooked), Knjiga je napisana prije sto godina.

Ending  Class            Examples
------  ---------------  ---------------------------
-an     -ati             napisati -> napisan
                         pročitati -> pročitan
                         prodati  -> prodan
-en     -iti (iotation)  učiniti  -> učinjen
                         baciti   -> bačen
                         zatvoriti-> zatvoren
        -jeti            vidjeti  -> viđen
        consonant stems  peći     -> pečen
                         donijeti -> donesen
                         jesti    -> jeden (pojeden)
-t      -eti/-uti/short  uzeti    -> uzet
                         početi   -> počet
                         zauzeti  -> zauzet
                         čuti     -> čut

Agreement: pečen kruh, pečena riba, pečeno meso
Passive:   Večera je skuhana. Stol je rezerviran.
  • Trgovina je zatvorena, a sve je već prodano. — The shop is closed, and everything is already sold.
  • Stol je rezerviran na moje ime. — The table is reserved in my name.
  • Ova knjiga je napisana prije sto godina. — This book was written a hundred years ago.
  • Mjesto je, nažalost, zauzeto. — The seat is, unfortunately, taken.
Corrections: _______________________________

The present verbal adverb (glagolski prilog sadašnji)

The present verbal adverb expresses an action happening at the same time as the main verb, English '-ing' clauses: Slušajući glazbu, učim (Listening to music, I study). It is formed only from imperfective verbs by adding -ći to the 3rd person plural present: čitaju → čitajući, rade → radeći, pišu → pišući, budu → budući (which also became the adjective 'future' and the conjunction budući da, 'since'). The form never changes, it does not agree with anything. In standard usage its unexpressed subject must be the same as the subject of the main clause; it belongs mostly to written and careful spoken language, where it replaces a dok-clause: Dok putujem, čitam = Putujući čitam.

3rd pl. present + -ći  ->  verbal adverb
---------------------------------------
čitaju   -> čitajući    (while) reading
rade     -> radeći      (while) working
pišu     -> pišući      (while) writing
slušaju  -> slušajući   (while) listening
putuju   -> putujući    (while) travelling
budu     -> budući      being (budući da = since)

Only from imperfective verbs; form never changes.
Same subject rule:
Putujući vlakom, čitala je novine. (she travels, she reads)
  • Slušajući radio, saznao sam novosti. — Listening to the radio, I learned the news.
  • Radeći svaki dan, brzo je napredovala. — Working every day, she progressed quickly.
  • Budući da nemam auto, putujem vlakom. — Since I don't have a car, I travel by train.
Corrections: _______________________________

Verbal nouns (glagolske imenice)

Verbal nouns name the action itself ('reading', 'swimming') and are formed from the passive-participle stem plus -je: čitati → čitanje, pisati → pisanje, učiti → učenje, putovati → putovanje, kupiti → kupnja/kupovanje. Most are built from imperfective verbs and are neuter nouns of the more type, declining regularly (bez čitanja, u pisanju). They are extremely productive in notices, schedules and formal style (parkiranje zabranjeno, radno vrijeme, znanje jezika), and often correspond to an English gerund or noun in '-ing'/'-tion'. Where a shorter noun exists (odluka 'decision' from odlučiti), the verbal noun in -nje still names the process rather than the result (odlučivanje 'decision-making').

Verb          Verbal noun    Meaning
------------  -------------  ------------------
čitati        čitanje        reading
pisati        pisanje        writing
učiti         učenje         learning, studying
plivati       plivanje       swimming
putovati      putovanje      travelling, trip
parkirati     parkiranje     parking
znati         znanje         knowledge
piti          piće           drink
(process vs result)
odlučiti -> odluka (result) / odlučivanje (process)
Declines as neuter: bez učenja, u putovanju, znanjem
  • Učenje jezika zahtijeva strpljenje. — Learning a language requires patience.
  • Parkiranje je ovdje zabranjeno. — Parking is forbidden here.
  • Bez znanja hrvatskoga teško je naći posao u struci. — Without knowledge of Croatian it is hard to find a job in one's profession.
Corrections: _______________________________

Subjectless sentences (besubjektne rečenice)

Some Croatian sentences have no subject at all, not even an implied one; the verb stands in the 3rd person singular neuter. They describe natural phenomena (Grmi, it's thundering, Sviće, dawn is breaking, Smrkava se, it's getting dark), existence and absence with nema/nije bilo/neće biti + genitive (Nema kruha, there is no bread, Nije bilo struje, there was no electricity), and states with adverbs (Kasno je, Bilo je lijepo). In the past these verbs take the neuter participle: Grmjelo je cijelu noć. The nema + genitive pattern is essential: it is how Croatian says 'there isn't/aren't', and its past and future are nije bilo and neće biti, all with the genitive.

Type              Present         Past
----------------  --------------  ------------------
weather           Grmi.           Grmjelo je.
                  Sviće.          Svanulo je.
                  Smrkava se.     Smrkavalo se.
existence (+ G!)  Ima kruha.      Bilo je kruha.
absence (+ G!)    Nema kruha.     Nije bilo kruha.
                  Nema ga.        Nije ga bilo.
     future:      Neće biti problema.
state + adverb    Kasno je.       Bilo je kasno.
                  Vruće je.       Bilo je vruće.
  • Cijelu noć je grmjelo i padala je kiša. — It thundered all night and it rained.
  • U trgovini nema svježeg kruha. — There is no fresh bread in the shop.
  • Jučer ga nije bilo na poslu. — He wasn't at work yesterday.
Corrections: _______________________________

Conditional sentences (pogodbene rečenice s ako, kad i da)

Croatian has three types of conditional sentence, each with its own conjunction pattern. Real conditions (likely, future) use ako with the present or futur II in the if-clause and futur I or an imperative in the main clause: Ako budeš učio, položit ćeš. Potential conditions (imaginable but hypothetical) use kad or ako with kondicional I in both clauses: Kad bih imao novca, kupio bih stan. Unreal conditions (contrary to fact) use da with the present or perfekt in the if-clause and kondicional I in the main clause: Da sam znao, došao bih (If I had known, I would have come, but I didn't). The choice of conjunction is itself meaningful: da + indicative always signals that the condition is not fulfilled.

Type        If-clause               Main clause
----------  ----------------------  -----------------
1. real     ako + present/futur II  futur I / imper.
            Ako budeš učio,         položit ćeš ispit.
            Ako imaš vremena,       dođi!
2. potential kad/ako + kondicional  kondicional I
            Kad bih imao novca,     kupio bih stan.
            Ako bi htio,            mogao bi doći.
3. unreal   da + present/perfekt    kondicional I
            Da sam znao,            došao bih.
            Da imam vremena,        pomogao bih ti.

da + indicative = condition NOT fulfilled
  • Ako sutra bude sunčano, ići ćemo na izlet. — If it is sunny tomorrow, we will go on a trip.
  • Kad bih govorio hrvatski savršeno, radio bih kao prevoditelj. — If I spoke Croatian perfectly, I would work as a translator.
  • Da si me nazvao, došao bih po tebe. — If you had called me, I would have come to pick you up.
Corrections: _______________________________

3. Cheatsheet

1 · The alphabet is 100% phonetic

  • Croatian has 30 letters and every letter is ALWAYS pronounced the same way. Learn it once → you can read any word.
  • Special letters: č/ć = 'ch', š = 'sh', ž = 'zh', đ = soft 'j', dž = hard 'j', lj = 'ly' (as in miLLion), nj = 'ny' (as in caNYon), c = 'ts', j = 'y'.
  • No silent letters, no surprises. Spelling = sound, sound = spelling.
  • Stress never falls on the last syllable, in short words it's usually on the first.
LETTER  SOUND        EXAMPLE
c       ts           cipela (shoe)
č / ć   ch           čaj (tea), ćao (bye)
š       sh           škola (school)
ž       zh           žena (woman)
j       y            ja (I)
lj      ly           ljubav (love)
nj      ny           konj (horse)
dž / đ  j            džem (jam), đak (pupil)

Dobar dan — Good day (DOH-bar dahn)

Hvala — Thank you (HVAH-lah)

2 · Three genders & the dictionary form (nominative)

  • Nouns are masculine, feminine or neuter, and you can usually TELL from the ending.
  • Masculine: usually ends in a consonant (grad = city, stol = table).
  • Feminine: usually ends in -a (žena = woman, kava = coffee).
  • Neuter: usually ends in -o or -e (mlijeko = milk, more = sea).
  • There are NO articles, no 'a' or 'the'. 'Žena' means woman / a woman / the woman.
GENDER     TYPICAL END   EXAMPLE
masculine  consonant     grad, stol, prijatelj
feminine   -a            žena, kava, škola
neuter     -o / -e       mlijeko, more, dijete

Ovo je kava. — This is coffee.

To je grad. — That is a city.

3 · Personal pronouns & 'to be' (biti)

  • ja (I), ti (you), on/ona/ono (he/she/it), mi (we), vi (you pl./formal), oni/one (they).
  • biti has a SHORT form (unstressed, used in normal sentences) and a long/negative form.
  • Pronouns are often dropped because the verb ending shows who: 'Sam' already implies 'I am'.
  • Negative of biti is one word: nisam, nisi, nije…
          SHORT   NEGATIVE
ja        sam     nisam
ti        si      nisi
on/ona    je      nije
mi        smo     nismo
vi        ste     niste
oni       su      nisu

Ja sam student. — I am a student.

Ona nije ovdje. — She is not here.

4 · Present tense of verbs

  • Drop the infinitive -ti and add personal endings: -m, -š, (none), -mo, -te, -ju/-e.
  • Most verbs follow predictable -a / -i / -e patterns: raditi (to work), govoriti (to speak), učiti (to study).
  • Like biti, the ending tells you the subject, so pronouns are optional.
  • Example raditi (to work): radim, radiš, radi, radimo, radite, rade.
RADITI (to work)
ja radim     mi radimo
ti radiš     vi radite
on radi      oni rade
(ending shows the subject)

Govorim malo hrvatski. — I speak a little Croatian.

Što radiš? — What are you doing?

5 · Cases: start with just TWO

  • Croatian has 7 cases, endings that change a noun depending on its ROLE in the sentence. Don't panic: master two first.
  • NOMINATIVE = the subject / dictionary form (the one DOING the action): 'Žena pije.' (The woman drinks.)
  • ACCUSATIVE = the direct object (the thing RECEIVING the action). Feminine -a → -u; masculine inanimate stays the same.
  • Because endings show the role, WORD ORDER is flexible, meaning stays clear even if you move words around.
  • The other 5 cases (genitive, dative, locative, instrumental, vocative) come later, one at a time.
ROLE        QUESTION   FEM EXAMPLE (kava)
nominative  who/what?  kava (subject)
accusative  what?      kavu  (object)
'Pijem kavu.' = I drink coffee.
(kava -> kavu because it's the object)

Žena pije kavu. — The woman drinks coffee. (žena = subject, kavu = object)

Volim Hrvatsku. — I love Croatia. (Hrvatska → Hrvatsku, object)

6 · Verb aspect: ongoing vs completed

  • Most Croatian verbs come in PAIRS: an imperfective (ongoing/repeated/process) and a perfective (single completed action).
  • Example: piti (to be drinking / drink habitually) vs popiti (to drink up completely).
  • Imperfective = the movie of the action; perfective = the snapshot of it finished.
  • You don't need every pair now, just notice the concept; it replaces a lot of English tense machinery.
ASPECT         MEANING            EXAMPLE
imperfective   ongoing/habitual   pisati (to write)
perfective     completed once     napisati (to write up)

Pišem pismo. — I am writing a letter. (in progress)

Napisao sam pismo. — I wrote (finished) the letter.

7 · The past tense (perfekt)

  • Everyday past = short form of biti (sam, si, je…) + the active past participle.
  • The participle ends in -o (m), -la (f), -lo (n), plural -li/-le, and AGREES with the subject's gender.
  • 'Radio sam' = I worked (man speaking); 'Radila sam' = I worked (woman speaking).
  • Negative: swap to the negative biti: 'Nisam radio' = I didn't work.
biti + participle (agrees with gender)
Radio sam   (I worked - male)
Radila sam  (I worked - female)
Radili smo  (we worked - plural)

Jučer sam bio u gradu. — Yesterday I was in the city. (male speaker)

Što si rekla? — What did you say? (to a female)

8 · The future (futur)

  • Future = short form of htjeti (to want): ću, ćeš, će, ćemo, ćete, će + the infinitive.
  • 'Ja ću raditi' = I will work. The 'ću' part can attach to the verb: 'Radit ću'.
  • It's regular and reuses the infinitive you already know.
  • Negative: neću, nećeš, neće… 'Neću raditi' = I won't work.
htjeti (short) + infinitive
ja ću        mi ćemo
ti ćeš       vi ćete
on će        oni će
'Ja ću učiti hrvatski.' = I will study Croatian.

Sutra ću raditi. — Tomorrow I will work.

Hoćeš li doći? — Will you come?

9 · Numbers, questions & survival

  • 0-10: nula, jedan, dva, tri, četiri, pet, šest, sedam, osam, devet, deset.
  • Question words: tko (who), što (what), gdje (where), kada (when), zašto (why), kako (how), koliko (how much).
  • Yes/no question: add 'li' after the verb, 'Govoriš li engleski?' (Do you speak English?).
  • Essential politeness: molim (please/you're welcome), hvala (thanks), oprostite (excuse me), da/ne (yes/no).

Gdje je kolodvor? — Where is the station?

Koliko košta? — How much does it cost?

10 · Glue words & first phrases

  • Connectors: i (and), ali (but), jer (because), pa/onda (so/then), s/sa (with), za (for).
  • Greetings: Bok / Dobar dan (hi/good day), Kako si? (How are you?), Doviđenja (goodbye).
  • 'Ja sam…' + name/nationality starts any introduction.
  • Don't fear mistakes, Croatians are delighted anyone tries their language.

Bok, ja sam Marko. Kako si? — Hi, I'm Marko. How are you?

Ne govorim dobro, ali učim. — I don't speak well, but I'm learning.

4. Quizzes (answers shown for review)

A0 — A0, Survival Croatian

1. How do you say 'Good day' in Croatian?

Answer: Dobar dan

'Dobar dan' = good day (the standard daytime greeting). 'Laku noć' = good night, 'Doviđenja' = goodbye, 'Hvala' = thank you.

2. Which word means 'thank you'?

Answer: Hvala

'Hvala' = thank you. 'Molim' = please/you're welcome, 'Oprostite' = excuse me, 'Bok' = hi/bye.

3. The letter 'š' is pronounced like...

Answer: sh in 'ship'

Croatian is phonetic: š = 'sh', č/ć = 'ch', ž = 'zh', j = 'y'. 'škola' = SHKOH-lah (school).

4. Complete the introduction: 'Ja ___ Marko.' (I am Marko)

Answer: sam

biti short forms: ja sam, ti si, on je... With 'ja' it's 'sam'. 'Ja sam Marko' = I am Marko.

5. What gender is 'žena' (woman)?

Answer: feminine

Nouns ending in -a are usually feminine. Consonant endings → masculine; -o/-e → neuter.

6. Write the number 'three' in Croatian.

Answer: tri

0-5: nula, jedan, dva, tri, četiri, pet. 'Tri' = three.

7. Choose the negative of 'je' (is): 'Ona ___ ovdje.' (She is NOT here)

Answer: nije

biti has one-word negatives: nisam, nisi, nije, nismo, niste, nisu. For 'ona' (she) it's 'nije'.

8. Conjugate raditi (to work) for 'ja': 'Ja ___.'

Answer: radim

Present endings: -m, -š, (none), -mo, -te, -e/ju. raditi → radim, radiš, radi, radimo, radite, rade.

9. Croatian has no articles. So 'kuća' can mean...

Answer: a house / the house / house

There is no 'a' or 'the' in Croatian. Context tells you which English article fits. 'kuća' = (a/the) house.

10. Order the words: 'I speak a little Croatian.'

Answer: Govorim malo hrvatski

The verb 'govorim' already means 'I speak' (no pronoun needed). 'malo' = a little, 'hrvatski' = Croatian.

A1 — A1, Everyday Croatian

1. Conjugate imati (to have) for 'ja': 'Ja ___ brata.' (I have a brother)

Answer: imam

imati: imam, imaš, ima, imamo, imate, imaju. With 'ja' → 'imam'.

2. Put 'kava' (coffee, feminine) into the accusative: 'Pijem ___.' (I drink coffee)

Answer: kavu

Feminine -a nouns change to -u in the accusative (the object). 'Pijem kavu' = I drink coffee.

3. Make a yes/no question: 'Govoriš engleski' → ?

Answer: Govoriš li engleski?

Add 'li' right after the verb to form a yes/no question: 'Govoriš li engleski?' = Do you speak English?

4. Negate the verb: 'Ja ___ razumijem.' (I do NOT understand)

Answer: ne

Regular verbs negate with 'ne' before the verb: 'Ne razumijem' = I don't understand. (biti is the exception with nisam etc.)

5. Choose the future tense: 'Sutra ___ raditi.' (Tomorrow I will work)

Answer: ću

Future = short htjeti (ću, ćeš, će...) + infinitive. 'Ja ću raditi' / 'Radit ću' = I will work.

6. Past tense, male speaker: 'Jučer ___ radio.' (Yesterday I worked)

Answer: sam

Perfekt = short biti (sam, si, je...) + participle. 'Radio sam' = I worked (man). A woman says 'Radila sam'.

7. Which past participle is correct for a FEMALE speaker saying 'I worked'?

Answer: radila

The participle agrees with gender: -o (m), -la (f), -lo (n), -li/-le (pl). A woman says 'radila sam'.

8. Genitive: 'a glass of water', complete 'čaša ___.' (voda → genitive)

Answer: vode

Feminine -a → -e in the genitive. 'čaša vode' = a glass of water. Genitive expresses 'of'.

9. Aspect: which verb means a COMPLETED action ('to drink up')?

Answer: popiti

piti (imperfective) = to be drinking / drink habitually; popiti (perfective, with prefix po-) = to drink up completely.

10. Order the words: 'The woman drinks coffee.' (use the correct cases)

Answer: Žena pije kavu

'Žena' stays nominative (the subject), 'kavu' is accusative (the object), 'pije' = drinks. Word order is flexible, but this is the neutral order.

A2 — A2, Cases, aspect & tenses

1. Genitive of possession: 'This is the friend ___.' (of my brother, brat → genitive)

Answer: brata

Masculine nouns add -a in the genitive: brat → brata. The genitive expresses 'of' / possession: 'prijatelj moga brata'.

2. Locative (location): 'I live in the city.' Complete: 'Živim u ___.' (grad → locative)

Answer: gradu

After 'u/na' meaning a static location, use the locative: grad → gradu. 'Živim u gradu' = I live in the city.

3. Which verb is PERFECTIVE (a single completed action)?

Answer: napisati

napisati (with prefix na-) is perfective = to write and finish. pisati is imperfective = to be writing / write habitually.

4. Past tense, female speaker: 'Jučer sam ___ u školi.' (was, biti participle, feminine)

Answer: bila

The past participle agrees with gender: bio (m), bila (f), bilo (n). A woman says 'bila sam' = I was.

5. Dative (to whom): 'I'm giving the book to my friend.' 'Dajem knjigu ___.' (prijatelj → dative)

Answer: prijatelju

The dative marks the recipient ('to/for'): prijatelj → prijatelju. 'Dajem knjigu prijatelju' = I give the book to my friend.

6. Match each case to what it marks.

Answer: nominative → the subject; accusative → the direct object; genitive → possession / &#x27;of&#x27;; dative → the recipient / &#x27;to&#x27;

Each case marks a role: nominative = subject, accusative = direct object, genitive = of/possession, dative = recipient. Endings change to show the role.

7. Future tense: 'Tomorrow I will study.' Choose: 'Sutra ___ učiti.'

Answer: ću

Future = short htjeti (ću, ćeš, će...) + infinitive: 'Ja ću učiti' / 'Učit ću'.

8. Instrumental ('with'): 'I travel with a friend.' 'Putujem s ___.' (prijatelj → instrumental)

Answer: prijateljem

The instrumental marks 'with' / means: prijatelj → prijateljem (masculine -em after a soft consonant). 's prijateljem' = with a friend.

9. Comparative: 'Croatia is ___ than Slovenia.' (bigger, velik)

Answer: veći

Comparative of velik is irregular: veći (bigger). najveći is the superlative (biggest). Use 'nego/od' for 'than'.

10. Order the words: 'Yesterday I drank coffee in a café.' (past + accusative + locative)

Answer: Jučer sam pio kavu u kafiću

Past = 'sam pio' (male). 'kavu' is accusative (object), 'kafiću' is locative (location after 'u'). Three systems working together.

B1 — B1, Full cases, conditional & nuance

1. Conditional ('would'): 'I would like a coffee.' Choose: 'Ja ___ kavu.'

Answer: bih htio

The conditional = aorist of biti (bih, bi, bi, bismo, biste, bi) + participle. 'Htio bih kavu' = I would like a coffee (polite).

2. Vocative (addressing): call out to Marko. 'Hej, ___!'

Answer: Marko

Many masculine names like Marko keep the same form in the vocative, but most masculine nouns change: prijatelj → prijatelju! The vocative is only for addressing someone.

3. Which case after the preposition 'iz' (out of)? 'Dolazim iz ___.' (grad)

Answer: grada (genitive)

'iz' (from/out of) always takes the genitive: iz grada = out of the city. Many prepositions govern a fixed case.

4. Plural accusative: 'I see the children.' 'Vidim ___.' (djeca → accusative)

Answer: djecu

'djeca' (children) is a collective noun behaving like a feminine singular: accusative djecu. 'Vidim djecu' = I see the children.

5. Aspect choice: 'I read (and finished) the book yesterday.' Pick the verb.

Answer: pročitao sam

A completed, whole action takes the perfective: pročitati → pročitao sam. 'čitao sam' (imperfective) means 'I was reading / used to read'.

6. Match each preposition to the case it governs.

Answer: iz (from) → genitive; u (into, motion) → accusative; u (in, location) → locative; s (with) → instrumental

Prepositions govern specific cases, and some (like 'u') take different cases for motion (accusative) vs location (locative). This is central to B1 accuracy.

7. Dative plural: 'I'm helping my friends.' 'Pomažem ___.' (prijatelji → dative)

Answer: prijateljima

The dative plural ending is -ima for masculine/feminine: prijatelji → prijateljima. The verb 'pomagati' takes the dative.

8. Conditional 'if' sentence: 'If I had money, I would travel.' The 'would travel' part is...

Answer: putovao bih

Hypothetical result uses the conditional: 'Da imam novca, putovao bih.' (bih + participle).

9. Comparative + 'than': 'Zagreb is bigger than Split.' 'Zagreb je veći ___ Split.'

Answer: od

After a comparative, 'than' = 'od' (+ genitive) or 'nego'. 'veći od Splita' / 'veći nego Split'.

10. Order the words: 'I told my friend that I would come.' (dative + conditional)

Answer: Rekao sam prijatelju da ću doći

'prijatelju' is dative (told TO my friend); 'da ću doći' = that I will come. Croatian often uses the future where English uses 'would' in reported speech.

B2 — B2, Aspect, voice & clitics

1. Clitic placement (2nd position): which is correct for 'I gave it to him'?

Answer: Dao sam mu ga

Unstressed clitics cluster in second position in a fixed order: verb-aux 'sam', then dative 'mu', then accusative 'ga'. Clitic ordering is a hallmark B2 skill.

2. Aspect: 'I read for an hour (process, didn't necessarily finish).' 'Sat vremena sam ___.' (čitati, male)

Answer: čitao

A process over a span uses the imperfective: 'čitao sam' (was reading). The perfective 'pročitao' would imply completion of the whole book.

3. Passive (participle): 'The letter ___ yesterday.' (was written, pismo, neuter)

Answer: je napisano

The passive uses biti + passive participle agreeing with the subject: pismo (neuter) → 'napisano'. 'Pismo je napisano' = the letter was written.

4. Genitive plural: 'a lot of books', 'puno ___.' (knjiga → genitive plural)

Answer: knjiga

Many feminine -a nouns have a zero-ending genitive plural identical to nominative singular: knjiga. Quantities take the genitive: 'puno knjiga'.

5. Reflexive 'se' for impersonal: 'How ___ this said in Croatian?'

Answer: se kaže

The reflexive 'se' forms impersonal/passive-like statements: 'Kako se kaže...?' = How does one say / how is it said...?

6. Match each imperfective verb to its perfective partner.

Answer: pisati → napisati; kupovati → kupiti; govoriti → reći; dolaziti → doći

Aspect pairs are often unpredictable: some add a prefix (pisati/napisati), some change the root (govoriti/reći, dolaziti/doći). Learning pairs together is essential at B2.

7. Conditional perfect: 'I would have come.' Choose:

Answer: bio bih došao

The past conditional = bio/bila + bih + participle: 'bio bih došao' = I would have come. 'došao bih' is the present conditional ('I would come').

8. Instrumental of means without preposition: 'I write with a pen.' 'Pišem ___.' (olovka → instrumental)

Answer: olovkom

The bare instrumental (no preposition) expresses the means/tool: olovka → olovkom. 'Pišem olovkom' = I write with a pen. ('s' is only for accompaniment.)

9. Which preposition+case for 'I'm going to the doctor's' (a person, motion to)?

Answer: kod liječnika (genitive)

Motion to a person uses 'kod' + genitive (idem kod liječnika), or 'k' + dative (idem k liječniku). You don't use 'u/na' with people the way you do with places.

10. Order the clitic cluster: 'I have already given it to her.'

Answer: Već sam joj ga dao

After the first word 'Već', the clitic chain follows in fixed order: aux 'sam' → dative 'joj' → accusative 'ga', then the participle 'dao'.

C1 — C1, Style, idiom & subtlety

1. Recognise the tense: 'Bijah umoran.' What is 'bijah'?

Answer: imperfect (imperfekt)

The imperfekt (bijah = I was) is an archaic/literary past, now rare in speech but met in literature and elevated style. C1 means recognising it.

2. The aorist survives in speech mainly with which verb? 'Rekoh ti!'

Answer: reći (I said/told)

Though largely literary, the aorist lingers colloquially in fixed forms like 'rekoh' (I said) and 'dođoh'. Spotting it is a C1 reading skill.

3. Idiom: complete 'Pada kiša kao iz ___.' (raining as if from buckets/'a jug')

Answer: kabla

'Kao iz kabla' = (pouring) as if from a bucket, the Croatian equivalent of 'raining cats and dogs'. Idiom is central to C1.

4. Verbal adverb (gerund): 'Reading the book, he fell asleep.' Choose 'reading'.

Answer: Čitajući

The present verbal adverb (glagolski prilog sadašnji) ends in -ći: 'čitajući' = while reading. It compresses a simultaneous clause, marking polished style.

5. Word formation: give the noun meaning 'freedom' that corresponds to the adjective 'slobodan' (free).

Answer: sloboda

slobodan (free, adj.) → sloboda (freedom, noun). C1 involves productive word-formation: recognising and building related words across parts of speech.

6. Match each idiom to its meaning.

Answer: trla baba lan → idle/pointless activity; muha bez glave → headless chicken (panicked); drži mi se → hang in there; ni luk jeo ni luk mirisao → to feign total innocence

Native idioms with no literal English equivalent are a clear C1 marker; using them naturally signals near-native command.

7. Choose the stylistically richer synonym for 'velik' (big) meaning 'enormous':

Answer: golem

C1 means a graded vocabulary: 'golem' (enormous) is a stronger, more vivid choice than the neutral 'velik'. Lexical precision matters.

8. Ekavian vs Ijekavian: the Croatian (ijekavian) word for 'milk' is 'mlijeko'; give the word for 'child'.

Answer: dijete

Standard Croatian is ijekavian (mlijeko, dijete) vs Serbian ekavian (mleko, dete). Controlling this reflex distinguishes polished Croatian at C1.

9. Which shows correct fronting for emphasis ('It's HIM I saw')?

Answer: Njega sam vidio.

Croatian's flexible word order lets you front the stressed full pronoun 'njega' for emphasis, with the clitic 'sam' still in second position.

10. Order this elevated sentence: 'Although tired, he kept working.' (verbal adverb + clitic)

Answer: Iako umoran, nastavio je raditi

An elliptical concessive ('Iako umoran' = although [he was] tired) plus the clitic 'je' in second position of the main clause, concise, native-like phrasing.
